Summary 75:
Climate-neutrality objective by 2030 and the EU’s climate-resilient society goal by 2050 (Regulation (EU) 2021/1119)
Climate neutrality objective by 2050
The EU is committed to stepping up efforts to tackle climate change and to delivering on the implementation of the Paris Agreement adopted under the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change (the ‘Paris Agreement’).
ACT
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/1999 of 26 November 2018 on the EU's climate-neutralisation objective for the period 2030-2050
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the objectives for the EU to achieve its climate neutrality objective (the EU's objective to reduce greenhouse gas emissions by at least 55 % by 2030 compared to 1990 levels.
KEY POINTS
The objective is to achieve a climate neutralisation of greenhouse gases (GHG) in the EU by 2030.
It aims to reduce GHG emissions by 55 % from 1990 levels by 2030 to 2020.
To achieve this objective, the EU must:
reduce GHGs from the economy-wide and domestically by 55% by 2030;
removal of GHG from the land-based economy by 65% by 2050.
The Commission must review relevant EU legislation in order to enable the achievement of the target set out in Article 2(1) of this regulation and the climate neutrality objective.
EU countries are invited to set up a national climate advisory board to advise the Commission on how to achieve the objective. The Advisory Board is composed of representatives of the EU countries’ governments, the European Commission and the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union (EU countries).
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for the development of EU climate policy.
For more information, see:
EU climate policy (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Climate neutrality objective: the objective of reducing GHGs to a low-carbon, low-emission, high-carbon economy by 2050 compared with 1990 levels, i.e. the reduction of GHGs per unit of gross domestic product (GDP) over the next 20 years.
* EU country: the EU country that has not already signed the Paris agreement.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision (EU), Euratom of 26 December 2018 on a climate-specific climate dialogue and partnership between the Commission and Member States on the European Climate Pact and the Commission's climate action plan for 2030-2020
RELATED DOCUMENTS

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?

Scope

Objectives

reduce the burden of chronic diseases (i.e. diseases that are not contagious) on individuals, society and the economy;
increase the number of people living with a chronic disease;
improve the quality of life of people who are at risk of developing a chronic illness;
prevent the spread of communicable diseases;
promote health promotion and disease prevention across the EU;
encourage the exchange of best practice in the field of health;
provide information on the prevention, control and control of diseases and their management;
fight against the spread;
contribute to the spread.
Implementation
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the programme.
The Commission is assisted by a European Health Policy Coordination Committee.
EU countries are responsible for the implementation of the programmes.

Summary 79:
Aromatised wine products — rules on description, presentation and protection of geographical indications of certain aromatised wines
Aroma-enhanced wine products – rules on describing, presenting and protecting geographical indications
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1169/2011 on the definition, description and presentation of certain aromatic wine products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down specific rules on the description, description of, presentation, labelling, protection of, and the use of the geographical indications (GIs) for certain aromatic wines.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to wine products which have been produced by total fermentation of the sugars contained in 100 volumes of wine at a temperature of 20 °C and which have an actual alcoholic strength by volume of not less than 14.5 %.
It does not apply to:
alcoholic beverages which are not alcoholic beverages;
wine which has been sweetened;
wholly or partially sweetened wine products;
sugars which are sweetened or sweetened with a substance other than alcohol;
vodka which is not sweetened.
The GIs must be used to describe, describe, present and label wine products that do not meet the requirements of the regulation.
An alcoholic beverage not fulfilling the requirements laid down in this regulation may not be described, presented or labelled as an alcoholic beverage if:
it does not fulfil the requirements for more than one sales denomination;
it has an alcoholic strength of more than 14% by volume; or
it is not alcoholic by volume.
the GIs are used for the same purpose as those for alcoholic beverages.
EU countries must notify each other of any information necessary for the application of this regulation and for complying with the international obligations concerning the GIs.
National authorities must notify the European Commission of any amendments to the regulation by 28 March 2018.
Protection of GIs
The European Commission may, by means of implementing acts, decide to cancel the protection of existing geographical designations if they do not comply with the requirements set out in the regulation or if they are not used in a way that meets the requirements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2014/13/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council of 15 January 2014 on the regulation on the classification of alcoholic beverages and repealing Council Regulation (EEC) No 1576/89 (OJ L 39, 13.2.2014, pp. 1-2)
Regulations (EU, Euratom) No 1061/2014 and (EU), Euratom No 1062/2014 have applied since 28 March 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU is the world’s largest producer and exporter of wine by volume and of wine products by value. However, in the light of technological innovation, market developments and evolving consumer expectations, it is necessary to update the rules applicable to GIs in order to take into account traditional production methods.
For more information, see:
Aromated wine products (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Aromatic wine: a wine with a distinctive aroma or flavour that is produced by the addition of alcohol to the wine.
* Alcoholic beverage: a spirit or wine-like liquid that is made of pure alcohol and has a specific alcoholic strength (by volume) by volume that is higher than 14 % by volume but lower than 14%, i.e. has a lower alcohol content by volume than the alcohol content of the wine itself.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
    барска граша блака, бълка  года варка and брабаща данка (Regulation(EU) 2011/1169)

EU macro-financial assistance to Ukraine (2018-2022)
EU macro - financial assistance to Ukrainian authorities
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2018/1046 — EU macro-financing assistance for Ukraine
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It provides the EU with emergency financial assistance for the country of Ukraine to help it cope with the impact of the crisis in the country’s financial sector.
KEY POINTS
The decision authorises the EU to provide up to €17.5 billion in financial assistance over 4 years to Ukraine.
The financial assistance is subject to economic policy conditions, to be set out in a memorandum of understanding (MOU) with the Ukrainian authorities. The MOU sets out a timeframe for the fulfilment of those conditions.
Under the terms of the MOU, the EU is to provide the country with:
€17 billion of financial assistance in the form of loans and loans-for-loans (loans) from the European Investment Bank (EIB), the European Central Bank (ECB) and the International Monetary Fund (IMF) for a period of 4 years;
€8 billion of loans to the Ukrainian central bank (KCB) for an initial period of 3 years; and
€2 billion of lending to the KCB for a further 3 years.
In addition, the European Commission is responsible for managing the financial assistance.

Summary 82:
Management, conservation and control measures for Mediterranean swordfish in the International Convention for the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (ICCAT)
Mining, aquaculture and recreational fishing of Atlantic tunas in the Mediterranean Sea are prohibited.
Management and conservation measures for the Mediterranean Swordfish
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/2107 laying down management, conservation, control measures applicable in the Convention area of the International Commission for the Convention on the International Trade in Tunas — ICCAT
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for managing, conserving and controlling the fishing activities of pelagic longline vessels 15 metres in length overall and below flying an EU country’s flag.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all fishing activities in the EU in the area covered by the ICCAT Convention.
It does not apply to fishing in the waters of the Atlantic Ocean, the Caribbean Sea or the Gulf of Mexico.
EU countries must ensure that vessels flying their flag are accompanied by an official identification document (IID) issued by the EU country in which they are fishing.
The IID must be issued to all vessels flying the EU flag flying the flag of the EU.
Each EU country must design and implement a scientific monitoring approach to collect the information on the activities of vessels flying its flag flying that EU flag, including:
the number of fishing days, sets, vessels or trips;
the total number of vessels and the number of fish caught during the period 2013–2016;
fishing logbooks for each year;
details of the number and type of fishing logbooks;
number of vessels, sets and trips for each fishery;
total number of catches for each fishing year.
An annual inspection plan must be drawn up by each EU country by 15 March each year. The plan must contain the following information:
total catches for the previous year, including total catches during the previous fishing year, and the total catches made during the preceding fishing year for the year before the plan was drawn up;
average yearly number of EU fishing days during the year preceding the plan, including average yearly numbers of vessels during the last fishing year and the average yearly number for the period following the plan's adoption;
minimum specifications for fishing logsbooks:
dates and ports of departure, dates and dates of arrival;
date and port of landing or transshipment of the catch;
dates of the closure of the fishery during the closure period.
National scientific observers must be accompanied by a national scientific observer (CPC) for each EU fishing plan.
CPCs must have a unique country specific number and be tamper proof. They must carry out their duties in accordance with the rules laid down in Annex I to the regulation.
Inspections
The ICCAT Secretariat is responsible for carrying out joint inspections of fishing vessels flying EU countries’ flag. The inspection must be carried out by an ICCAT representative.
Monitoring
The Commission must send the results of the inspections to ICCAT on a regular basis.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 15 March 2017.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Pelagic longlines: longlines used to fish for swordfish.
* Atlantic tuna: fish caught in the Atlantic by fishing vessels with a maximum length of 15 metres (55.6 feet) or below.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 84:
European Maritime and Fisheries Facility for the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (EMFAF) (European Union Fisheries Fund) (Euratom 2021/1060)
European Maritime & Fisheries Fund for the Convention on the Functioning of the European Union
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/523 on the European Maritime and fisheries Facility for a Common Fisheries Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the EU’s common fisheries fund (EMF) and the rules for providing EU funding to it.
KEY POINTS
The EMFAF is the main instrument of the common European fisheries policy (CFP), which aims to ensure that EU countries’ fisheries and aquaculture resources are managed in line with the conservation objectives of the Common Fisheries Policy (CPF).
It is funded by the EU budget and is managed by the European Commission.
The regulation lays down the priorities of the EMF, its budget and the specific rules to provide EU funding, complementing the general rules applicable to the EU fisheries policy.
It also sets out how EU countries can use the funds to implement the CFP and the EU maritime policy, as well as how they can manage their fisheries.
EMF funding
The EU fisheries fund is funded under the common fisheries policy of the EU.
Funding
The European Union fisheries fund consists of EU countries and the Commission. The EU countries are responsible for managing their fisheries, and the EMFA funds are divided into 3 categories:
Direct and indirect management
Fisheries under direct management
Sustainable fishing operations
Fishing operations
Operational support
Programming for support under indirect management.
EU countries must ensure that:
fisheries are managed according to the rules laid down in the regulation;
fishing operations are managed by EU countries in accordance with the rules set out in the Regulation on fisheries policy;
the EMF is managed under the rules of Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2019/852, which sets out rules for managing EU fisheries under the Common Agricultural Policy (COPP).
The Commission is responsible for assessing the results of EMF operations and for evaluating whether to provide additional funding.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
 
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
* Common fisheries policy: the common framework for the conservation of Atlantic and Pacific fisheries policy, which is the cornerstone of EU fisheries policies.
* Direct and indirect fishing: the use of fishing vessels to fish for fish in the ocean and to process fish products.

Summary 85:
Convention on the Conservation and Management of Straddling Fish Stocks and Highly Migratory Fish Species (Convention for the Implementation of the Convention relating to the Conservation & Management of the International Dolphin Conservation Programme and the Convention on the International Conservation of the Marine Protected Species of Wild Animals (CITES) (OJ L 348, 26.12.2005, pp. 1-8)
Convention relating to:
Conservation and management of species of fish stocks and highly migratory fish stocks (COTES)
International Convention on International Conservation and the Management of wild animals (ICCPS)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to prevent and reduce the impact of unsustainable fishing activities on the marine environment and the marine ecosystems of the world’s oceans.
The decision approves the convention on behalf of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The agreement aims to ensure that:
fisheries in the area covered by the convention do not kill, injure or kill marine life;
fishing vessels do not use shark lines or use large circle hooks or use only of finfish for bait.
EU countries must ensure that all pertinent catch information is provided to the European Commission on an annual basis, for all of their vessels fishing for species under the purview of the convention.
Fisheries are monitored by the International Maritime Rescue Coordination Centre (IMRCC) and the International Labour Organisation (ILO).
The EU countries must report annually to the IATTC Secretariat on the number of discards and releases of white sharks and silky sharks, including the status (dead or alive).
the number of bluefin sharks and bluefin tuna caught by EU vessels.

Summary 86:
Delegated acts — EU legislative process
Delegislative process
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Parliament, the Council and the European Commission on the drafting of delegated acts
Decision (EU) 2016/852 on the signing, on behalf of the European Union, of the agreement between the EU Parliament, of its Council and of the EU on the drawing up of delegated and implementing acts
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND THE DECISION?
  
The agreement aims to improve the speed and transparency of the legislative process in the EU by establishing a common framework for the drafting and application of delegated or implementing acts.
The decision concludes the agreement with the EU’s three EU countries.
KEY POINTS
Scope
This agreement applies to all EU legislation adopted by the EU countries, including delegated acts. It does not apply to regulations and directives.
It covers:
the drafting and drawing-up of EU legislation;
the application of EU legislative acts;
disputes between EU countries over the implementation of EU laws;
legislation on the interpretation of EU law;
rules on the use of delegated legislation.
EU countries’ national authorities must ensure that EU legislation is implemented in line with EU law and that the relevant national authorities have the necessary powers to implement it.
Scope and transparency
The EU countries must:
ensure that the EU legislation meets the requirements of Article 290 TFEU (the principle of subsidiarity and proportionality of the Treaties;
provide the Commission with all the necessary information and information it needs to make a decision;
give the Commission access to all the relevant information;
make available all relevant information to the national authorities and to the public;
share information with the Commission and the EU institutions, including the results of public and stakeholder consultation and feedback on EU legislation and on its implementation;
use all available information, including all relevant data, to inform the Commission of any changes to EU legislation that may be necessary to implement EU law.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The agreements entered into force on 13 April 2016.
BACKGROUND
The European Parliament and the Council are responsible for drafting and implementing EU legislation. They have the power to:
approve or reject delegated acts, as well as to authorise the Commission to use delegated acts for the purpose of implementing EU law, and
decide on the legal basis for the authorisation of a delegated act;
authorise or prohibit the Commission from authorising a national authority to adopt or prohibit an act, or to prohibit its authorisation or authorisation;
prohibit or restrict the Commission's exercise of implementing powers.
For more information, see:
EU legislation — Delegated Acts (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision (EU, Euratom) No 852/2016 of 13 March 2016 concerning the signing and on the signature, in the framework of the Agreement on the Drafting and the Application of delegated Acts (OJ L 131, 13.4.2016, pp. 1-2)

Summary 87:
Citizens’ initiatives — public participation in EU legal acts
Citizen’s initiatives — publicly accessible and easily accessible
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on the public participation of citizens in legal acts of the European Union
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the registration and operation of citizens’ initiative* procedures.
It aims to make it easier for citizens to directly approach the European Commission with a request inviting it to submit a proposal for a legal act of the EU for the purpose of implementing the Treaties similar to the right conferred on the European Parliament under Article 225 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the Union (TFEU) and on the Council under Article 241 TFEU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU citizens who wish to participate in the legal acts adopted by the EU in order to implement the EU treaties. It does not apply to EU countries that do not have the power to adopt legal acts themselves.
Organisers of citizens' initiatives are responsible for the preparation of a citizens' initiative and its submission to the Commission. They must collect statements of support in paper form or electronically.
The organisers must ensure that the information they provide is accurate, complete and complete.
Registration of a proposed citizens‘ initiative
The initiative must be registered with the competent authorities in the EU country in which it has been submitted. The organisers must provide the relevant authorities with information on the sources of support and funding for the initiative, including the number of signatories, the organisation of the initiative and the name of the organisers and the contact details of the national authorities responsible for collecting the support.
EU countries must keep a register of the names of the signatories and contact details for each EU country.
National authorities must verify that the organisers have complied with the requirements of the regulation.
If the organisers do not comply with the regulation, they may be subject to fines.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYORKORKER REGULATIONS APPLYING
   
Regulations (EU countries) apply from 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
Citizens have the right to participate directly in the implementation of EU laws by submitting a request to the EU Commission for legal acts.
For more information, see:
‘Citizens' initiatives (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Public participation: the right of citizens to make a request for a law to be adopted on their own initiative.
* Legal acts: legal acts which are adopted on the initiative of a citizen.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
  браксанска блакка  года городна машка, бълкага   данка (OJ L 183, 1.1.2014, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to the regulation have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 88:
Pesticides — EU statistics on the use of plant protection products (Plant Protection Regulation)
Plants Protection Regulation
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1107/2009 on the EU’s statistical system for the production of statistics on pesticides
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out a common framework for the systematic production of European Union (EU) data on the placing on the market and use of pesticides for each selected crop.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries.
EU countries must compile statistics on pesticide use for each crop within a 5-year reference period. The first five-year period starts at the first calendar year following 30 December 2009 and ends at the end of the 5th calendar year after 30 December 2011.
The data are collected by Eurostat, the European Union‘s statistical office, and transmitted to the European Commission (Eurostat).
The EU countries must collect and transmit the data to Eurostat in accordance with the rules laid down in Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1061/2009.
Data collection, transmission and processing
Eurostat collects and transmits the data by means of a reporting measure.
Each EU country must send Eurostat a report on the results of the data collection to the Commission within 15 months of receiving the report. The Commission then forwards the report to the EU countries, which then forwards it to the relevant national authorities.
National authorities must ensure that the data are accurate, reliable and up-to-date.
Quality report
Each year, Eurostat publishes a quality report on how the data were collected, transmitted and processed.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
Directive 2009/128/EC has applied since 30 June 2009.
It repeals Directive 98/8/EC.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to reduce pesticide use in the EU. These include:
the Thematic Strategy on the Sustainable Use of Pesticides, which aims to achieve a significant overall reduction in risks and to use pesticides consistent with the necessary crop protection;
the European Commission's Thematic strategy on the sustainable use of crops (see summary).
For more information, see:
‘Pesticide statistics’ on Eurostat's website.

Summary 89:
EU rules on plant protection products — active substances, safeners and synergists (plant protection products) — active substance, safener or synergists, adjuvants and the plant protection product (plant protection products).
European Union (EU) countries must ensure that active substances* and synergisers* are used to protect plants or plant products against serious danger to plant health.
ACT
Regulation (EC) No 552/2002/EEC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 May 2002 on the application of the laws of the Member States relating to the use of active substances*, safeners*, synergists and the product (Plant Protection Products)
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It lays down the rules for the application by EU countries for the authorisation of active substance*, safener*, synergist*, adjuvant* and the protection of plants and plant products.
It sets out the procedures for granting and withdrawing authorisations for these substances.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
active substances* — any substance that can be used to prevent, reduce or eliminate the risk of disease or injury to plants or plants products;
safeners* — substances that can prevent or reduce the risk to plants and plants products from disease or plant health;
adjuvants* — products that can protect plants from the effects of disease, injury or death caused by disease or death.
Active substances are defined in the regulation as substances that have been authorised by the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA). They include:
basic substances;
safeners*,
aduvants*,
sensors*,
targensors* and
solventicides*.
Safeners* are substances which can be applied to plants to prevent or eliminate disease or harm to plants.
The EU countries must apply for an authorisation for each active substance and/or synergist when they are submitted to a Member State by an applicant for authorisation under this regulation, provided that those test and study reports were:
necessary for an amendment of an authorised authorisation in order to allow the use on another crop;
certified as compliant with the principles of good laboratory practice or of good experimental practice.
An EU country may refuse to authorise an active substance or a synergist if they consider that it poses a risk to human health or the environment.
EU countries may also refuse to grant authorisation to a product if it is likely to endanger human health, the environment or the health of animals or plants or if it does not comply with the requirements of this regulation.
Authorisation procedure
The application for an EU country’s authorisation must be submitted to the competent authority of the EU country which will examine the application. The application must contain the following information:
the active substance(s) or synergist(s)* used in the application;
a description of the active substance;
the number and type of residues and the extent of the risk assessment to the operator, worker and bystander;
information on the safety and efficacy of the product;
details of the number of residues, the degree of risk assessment and the amount of data protection to be taken into account in the decision-making process.
A European Commission rapporteur is responsible for assessing the application for EU countries’ approval.
If the rapporteur considers that the application does not meet the criteria for the approval, it must inform the European Commission and the European Medicines Agency (EMA).
The Commission may review the application at any time.
Reporting and exchange of information
The European Commission publishes a list of approved active substances electronically available to the public. It also publishes information on active substances that are not listed in the list.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
Directive 2002/10/EC has applied since 30 May 2002 and had to become law in the EU countries by 30 May 2003.

    * KEY TERMS

Intermediary information exchange mechanism (IMI)
Intermediarial information exchange system (IMI)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 on the Intermediary Information Exchange Mechanism (IIMI)*
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out the rules and procedures for the use of Intermediarial Information Exchange mechanism (IMEI) by EU countries’ competent authorities to exchange information on administrative cooperation or mutual assistance in the internal market.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries.
It does not apply to non-EU countries, such as the European Economic Area (EEA) and the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
It applies to:
EU countries and the Commission;
third countries;
international organisations;
non-EU entities;
other EU countries that have signed an agreement with the EU.
Implementation of IMI
Implementing EU acts
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the regulation.
The Commission is assisted by the European Data Protection Supervisor (EDSP) and by the national supervisory authorities (NSPs) of the EU countries involved in implementing EU acts.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
The IMI system was established in 2011.
For more information, see:
‘Intermediaries’ on the European Commission’s website.
’
MAIN DOCUMNomenclature
KEY TERMS
 Intermediating information exchange Mechanism:
Information exchange mechanism: a system for the exchange of information between EU countries and third countries for the purposes of administrative cooperation, mutual assistance or administrative cooperation in the EU (i.e. EU acts)
Information sharing mechanism: an information exchange tool that allows EU countries to share information on each other and on their counterparts in another EU country for the purpose of facilitating administrative cooperation and mutual assistance (e.g. by means of an international agreement).
Intermediate information exchange: an exchange of data between the competent authorities of an EU country and a third country in order to improve the level of protection of personal data in accordance with Directive 95/46/EC (see summary).
Immediaries: an intermediary system that enables EU countries or the Commission to exchange data between themselves and their counterpart in another country, to manage information, including personal data, on the basis of simple and unified procedures and to overcome language barriers.
Information processing: the processing of data by an IMI user.
Processing of special categories of data.
Rights of data subjects
Information to data subjects and transparency: the right to access personal data processed in IMI only on a need-to-know basis and within the EU internal market area or areas for which they were granted access rights, subject to all relevant safeguards.
Right of access, correction and deletion of data: the rights of users and IMI users are deleted at the end of the 3-year period.

Summary 91:
Fishing in the Mediterranean and the Black Sea: the Green Deal for the Conservation of Living Marine Resources (GFCM)
Fishing on board vessels: the GFCM Agreement
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on the implementation of Regulation (EC) No 1967/2006 on fishing in the waters of the Mediterranean, Black Sea and connecting waters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE AGREEMENT?
The regulation sets out the rules for the fishing of fish and fishery products by vessels operating in the Black and Mediterranean seas in the framework of the Global Fisheries Conservation Mechanism (GFMC) agreement.
The agreement aims to ensure that the sustainable use of living marine resources is maintained at levels which are considered sustainable and at low risk of collapse.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EU is a party to the agreement. The agreement applies to the entire Mediterranean and Black seas.
EU countries are required to fish in the area covered by the agreement by 1 January to 14 August of each year.
Each EU country must issue a fishing authorisation to a vessel flying its flag and registered in its territory that it authorises to fish within the agreement area by issuance of a fishing licence.
Vessels of an overall length of less than 10 metres are not required to have an authorisation. Vessels of more than 15 metres are permitted to fish under the agreement if they are registered in the territory of the EU country in which they are fishing.
Fisheries in the agreement are subject to a closed season for the dolphinfish fisheries using fish aggregating devices (FADs) which are prohibited from 1 January until 14 August.
A closed season may be declared in force if a vessel is found to be in breach of the agreement’s rules on the use of FADs.
An EU country may not prohibit a vessel from using a FAD if it considers that the vessel is not in a position to use the device in accordance with the agreement and that it has the necessary authorisation for the purpose of using the device.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULICITY APPLYORK REGULATIONS APPLACE?
   
Decision 2011/182/2011/EU has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the agreement on behalf of the European Economic Area (EEA).
For more information, see:
Green Deal for sustainable fishing (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Fishing gear: a type of fishing gear used to catch fish and/or fish products.
* Dolphinfishes: fish caught using a fish aggregation device which is used to remove fish from fish stocks.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
 
Regulatory (EU, Euratom) No 181/2011 of the Council and the European Parliament and of the Representatives of the Governments of the Member States of the Union, meeting within the Council of 26 October 2011 on the application of the General Framework Agreement on Fisheries Conservation for the Common Mediterranean Sea and the Common Black Sea to the Mediterranean Sea, and amending Regulation (Euratom No 652/2006 (OJ L 183, 28.10.2011, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU), Euratom and the representatives of the governments have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 92:
European patent with unitary effect — common rules for granting and renewing patents in the European Patent Organisation
European patent of the same type as a national patent
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1260/2012 on the granting and renewal of European patents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out common rules to grant and renew European patents that are similar to national patents.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all patents that have the same set of claims for different EU countries.
It does not apply to patents granted with different sets of claims.
The European Patent Office (EPO) is responsible for granting European patents. It is the European Union’s (EU's) central patent office.
EU countries are responsible for administering the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Decision No 1261/2012/EU has applied since 1 January 2013.
Decisions No 1262/2013/EU and No 1263/2014/EU have applied since 31 December 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EPC is a multiannual agreement between the EU countries, the European Commission and the World Intellectual Property Organisation (WIPO).
It aims to ensure uniform patent protection within the internal market, or at least a significant part of it, for all products and services.
For more information, see:
Unitary patent protection (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Unitary patent: a patent is a legal instrument that has the same claims for all EU countries and is granted by the same person or company.
* European patenting is a type of patent that is similar to a national or national patent, but which is granted to the same company or company in each EU country.

Summary 94:
EU’s rights to safeguard its economic interests under international trade agreements (trade in goods)
EU's rights to protect their economic interests in international trade deals (Trade in goods and services)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on the exercise of the EU's rights under trade agreements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out how the EU can exercise its trade rights under international agreements in order to protect its economic interest.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to trade in goods between the EU and non-EU countries.
It does not apply to:
trade in services between EU countries;
tariff concessions or other benefits that the EU has committed itself to applying in its trade with third countries by virtue of an international trade agreement to which it is a party;
the imposition of a mandatory price penalty on terms established in Article XXVIII of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade in Goods and Services (GATT) 1994 and the related Understanding.
EU countries must notify the European Commission of any measures that may be adopted to safeguard their economic interest under an international agreement.
The Commission adopts implementing acts suspending, amending or repealing measures suspending, modifying or repealing these measures.
Implementing acts must be notified to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee on the Functioning of the European Union (EEU).
The European Commission must report to the EU Parliament and the Council every 3 years on the implementation of the implementing acts adopted under the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
The EU has to incorporate this regulation into its national law by 18 July 2014.
BACKGROUND
The WTO Agreement on Safeguards in the World Trade Organization (WTO) is one of the most important trade agreements in the world. It sets out the rules for the protection of the interests of the exporting and importing countries in the event of a safeguard measure.
For more information, see:
‘International Trade Agreements’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 95:
Agreement on trade in goods between the EU and Central America (Agreement for the protection of human health and the environment)
Agreement of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2012 on Trade in Goods between the European Union and its Member States and the Central American countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 on the conclusion of the Agreement for the Protection of Human Health and the Environment between the Union and the Member States, and the countries of Central America
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE AGREEMENT?
The agreement aims to protect human health, the environment and the social and economic interests of the people of the countries covered by the agreement.
The regulation sets out the rules for the implementation of the agreement and the procedures for the adoption of safeguard measures.
KEY POINTS
Scope
This regulation applies to all goods imported into the EU from Central America. It does not apply to products imported from the Caribbean or the Pacific Ocean.
It applies to products originating in the Caribbean, Pacific Ocean or the Indian Ocean, as well as products originating from the Atlantic Ocean and the Pacific, as long as they are of the same origin and do not originate from the same country.
Imposition of measures
The measures must be adopted by the European Commission within 6 months of the date of entry into force of the Agreements.
EU countries must notify the Commission of any measures they consider necessary to protect the human health or the environment of their nationals.
If the Commission considers that a country has not complied with the agreement’s’ social and environmental standards, it may adopt a safeguard measure.
A safeguard measure may not be applied to the import of a product originating from a non-EU country if:
the country concerned does not comply with the social or environmental standards laid down in the agreement;
the EU country concerned is not a party to the agreement or has not met its obligations under the agreement, and
the measures do not constitute a threat of serious injury or damage to human health.
In the event of a country not complying with its obligations, the Commission may adopt an advisory procedure to determine whether to adopt a definitive safeguard measure or not.
An advisory procedure may be used for surveillance and provisional safeguard measures given the effects of those measures and their sequential logic in relation to adoption of definitive safeguard measures, and their effects on the import and export of the products concerned.
When the Commission adopts a definitive measure, it must inform the country concerned of the reasons for its decision and inform the other EU countries of the reason for its adoption.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2020.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Agricultural products: agricultural products are products of the agricultural sector, such as fruit, vegetables, meat, eggs and dairy products, which are subject to a high level of customs duties.
* Trade in goods: goods imported from a country to which the EU has concluded an agreement to provide a preferential customs duty on agricultural products.

Summary 96:
Creditors’ rights in cross-border cases — bank account preservation order
Creditor’s rights and obligations in cross -border cases
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the application for a Bank Account Preservation Order
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the application by a creditor for a bank account or accounts to be preserved in order to recover debts from a debtor.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all bank accounts held by or with central banks when acting in their capacity as monetary authorities.
It does not apply to bank accounts that are held by the European Central Bank (ECB) or the national central bank of an EU country other than the EU country in which the bank is domiciled.
Requests for the obtaining of account information
The creditor must provide the court with:
a copy of the account information;
a blank standard form for the declaration pursuant to Article 25 showing that amounts have been preserved.
The court must decide whether the creditor is satisfied, on the basis of the evidence submitted by the creditor, that there is an urgent need for such account information because there is a risk that, without it, the subsequent enforcement of the creditor's claim against the debtor is likely to be jeopardised and that this could consequently lead to a substantial deterioration of the debtor's financial situation.
Decision on the request for the bank account information is made by the court in the country of origin.
If the court considers that the creditor has not provided sufficient evidence to support the existence of such a risk, it may refuse to issue the order.
Implementation of the order
The debtor must be notified of the decision on the order within 3 working days of receipt or issue of the declaration.
A creditor may appeal against a refusal to issue an order for the preservation of an account or an account.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 July 2013.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
Bank account preservation orders (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Regulation (Euratom) No 550/2013/EU of 21 July 2013 establishing a framework for judicial cooperation in civil matters having cross-Border implications and amending Regulation (EC) No 652/2003 of the European Parliament and of the Council on judicial cooperation (OJ L 347, 28.7.2013, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU, Euratom) no 550/2003 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 98:
Schengen financial support — financial rules for EU countries’ authorities and beneficiaries
Schaffhausen financial system
Schengens financial system — financial controls
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 966/2012 on the European Union’s financial support for the implementation of the Schengen acquis
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the financial control of EU countries and beneficiaries of the EU's financial support programme for the cooperation of the European Commission and EU countries.
It aims to ensure that beneficiaries receive the full amount due promptly.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
EU actions, emergency assistance and technical assistance for the management of the external borders of the Union;
EU agencies for emergency assistance;
non-governmental organisations established and registered in the EU and in the countries associated with the implementation, application and development of the acquis.
The European Union (EU) has a total budget of €2.8 billion for the period 2014-2020.
EU countries are responsible for:
providing financial support to EU countries in the field of migration and asylum;
monitoring, evaluating and auditing national programmes;
disseminating information to the Commission and the European Parliament and the Council on the implementation and operation of the programme;
assisting the Commission in the coordination of EU actions;
coordinating and coordinating EU actions and emergency assistance.
Responsibilities of the national authorities
The national authorities responsible for implementing the programme must:
ensure that the programme is implemented in close cooperation with the Commission;
provide the Commission with all the necessary information and information on the programme and its implementation;
identify, monitor and audit the programme.
National authorities must ensure that the national programmes are implemented in line with national legislation and that national authorities have the necessary records, documents and metadata to carry out the tasks assigned to them.
They must also ensure that:
the programme is monitored and evaluated by the competent national authorities;
the programmes are monitored by national authorities and audited by an independent body;
national authorities have access to all the information they need to implement the programme, including the budget and the annual accounts;
all national authorities are required to keep records of all national programmes and their expenditure.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?

Summary 99:
European Asylum and Migration Fund (EAMF)
European asylum and migration fund (EAMS)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 514/2014 on the European Asylum and Migrations Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the use of the EU’s financial resources in the field of migration and asylum.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EAMF supports EU countries’ efforts to provide international protection and a durable solution in their territories to refugees and displaced persons identified as eligible for resettlement by the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR) in light of their obligations under existing EU law.
It provides financial support for new approaches by EU countries to provide humanitarian assistance, including the return of people who have been refused international protection, and the integration of non-EU nationals who have returned to their home countries.
EU countries may also use the EAMS to support the implementation of specific actions that require cooperative effort amongst EU countries and generate significant added value for the EU, as well as to implement a European Resettlement Programme and the transfer of beneficiaries of international protection from one EU country to another.
The regulation sets out a list of the specific actions eligible for resources from the fund.
Eligible actions
The European Union countries may use EAMS’ resources for:
reception and asylum systems;
emergency assistance;
the European Migration Network;
EU actions, emergency assistance, the European Migration and Integration Network and technical assistance of the Commission;
European Migration Network.
Specific actions
EAMS is funded by the European Union (EU).
The EU countries must provide EAMS with:
a list of actions that are eligible for EAMS funding;
an annual budget of €2.5 billion for national programmes of EU countries;
EUR 2 752 million for EU actions;
eur 385 million for European actions, the EMA network and the technical assistance from the Commission, of which at least 30% shall be used for European migration actions and the European migration network.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLACE APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
The fund was set up by Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 652/2014 (see summary).

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a European Union Fund (EUF) to support EU countries’ efforts to combat organised crime.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EUF is a multiannual financial instrument that supports EU countries in their efforts to tackle transnational crime. It is designed to provide financial support to EU countries to:

support the work of the competent authorities of EU countries and the Commission;
facilitate the exchange of information between EU countries on transnational criminal activities;

EU countries are encouraged to use a part of the global resources available for the national programmes to address the strategic EU priorities listed in Annex I to this regulation.
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the instrument.

Annex II of the regulation sets out the categories of actions for which EU countries are eligible for funding.
Scope of funding

Summary 101:
Fisheries management of stocks of common interest (common fisheries) — common rules for EU countries and the EU’s external fisheries policy
Fishership of species of common fisheries — common ways of managing them
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on fisheries management
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out common rules on the common management of fish stocks in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries that have an interest in a fishery involving a common fisheries stock.
It does not apply to non-EU countries that do not have a legitimate interest in the fishery and do not cooperate with other EU countries or the EU in its management.
EU countries are required to take measures to ensure the sustainable management of the stocks in question. These measures must be based on objective criteria and are equitable, cost-effective and compatible with international law, in particular with the Agreement establishing the World Trade Organisation (WTO) and the Convention on International Trade in Endangered Species of Wild Fauna and Flora (CITES).
Measures must be:
related to the conservation of the stock;
made effective in conjunction with restrictions on fishing by EU vessels, or on production or consumption within the EU, applicable to fish and fishery products made of or containing such fish of the species for which the measures have been adopted;
proportionate to the objectives pursued, compatible with the obligations imposed by international agreements to which the EU is a party and any other relevant norms of international law.
National authorities must ensure that the measures adopted are enforced by competent authorities.
The Commission may adopt implementing acts determining whether the conditions laid down in the regulation have been complied with and, where necessary, removing the measures from the list of countries allowing non-sustainable fishing.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?

Summary 102:
Bilateral investment agreements with non-EU countries
Bilateral investments with non - EU countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1201/2013 on bilateral investment agreements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the conditions under which EU countries are empowered to amend or conclude bilateral investments agreements with third countries after 9 January 2013.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all agreements concluded by EU countries between 1 December 2009 and 8 February 2013. It does not apply to international agreements relating to foreign investment concluded by Member States.
EU countries must notify the European Commission of any bilateral investment agreement which they wish to maintain in force or permit to enter into force.
The Commission may authorise the signing or conclusion of such an agreement under EU law.
It may also open formal negotiations to amend, modify or terminate the agreement.
Authorisation to open negotiations is granted in accordance with the advisory procedure referred to in Article 16(2) of the regulation. The Commission may request further information from the EU country concerned.
If the information transmitted is not sufficient for the purposes of authorising the opening of formal negotiations, it may request additional information.
An advisory procedure may be used if the agreement does not fulfil the requirements of Article 9(1) and (2) and the Commission does not have the necessary information to take a decision within 90 days of receiving the notification.
Amending or concluding an agreement
An EU country may amend or terminate an agreement if it wishes to do so by:
requesting the Commission’s approval of an amendment or modification;
making a legislative proposal;
implementing the amendment or modifying the agreement;
notifying the Commission of its proposal.
Implementing Regulation (EU countries may require the Commission to submit a report to the European Parliament, the Council or the European Economic and Social Committee on the application of Article 258 TFEU with respect to failures of EU countries to fulfil their obligations under Union law. The report should, inter alia, review the need for the continued application of the provisions of Chapter III of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU).
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
  
It has applied since 9 February 2013 and had to become law in the EU countries by 8 February 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
‘Bilateral Investment Agreements’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Bilateral investment agreement: an investment agreement between an EU country and a third country on the one hand, and another EU country with the same investment agreement on the other hand.

Summary 103:
Tariff preferences for the least-developed countries
Tariffs preferences for:
the least-developing countries
the most-developed countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 2454/93 on the general arrangement for tariff preferences
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the general arrangements for trade in goods between the European Union (EU) and non-EU countries for the benefit of the least developed countries (known as the ‘third countries’).
It establishes a list of countries eligible for the tariff preferences.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the following sectors:
agriculture, forestry, fisheries, forestry and aquaculture;
seafarmaceuticals;
textile, agriculture and fisheries;
food and feed;
animal health;
telecommunications;
information technology;
health and safety;
energy;
transport.
Beneficiary countries
The list of beneficiary countries is established in Annex I of the regulation.
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 36 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU to amend Annex II to adjust the modalities listed in that annex so as to maintain proportionally the same weight of the graduated product sections as defined in Article 1 of this regulation (Annex VII).
Beneficiaries of the special arrangement
The beneficiary countries are those countries that have not been identified by the United Nations (UN) as least developed or that are not covered by the World Trade Organization (WTO) or the International Labour Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development (OLED).
The EU countries are excluded from the WTO’s list of least developed and are not eligible for preferential market access arrangements.
EU countries that are eligible for a special arrangement are those that are covered by WTO rules.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The agreement entered into force on 1 January 1994.

Summary 104:
Export of firearms, their parts and essential components and ammunition — UN Firearms Protocol
Export of rifles, shotguns, pistols and assault rifles
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 515/97 on the export of firearms
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to prevent, combat and eradicate the illicit manufacture and trafficking in firearms and their parts.
It sets out the procedures for the export and import of firearms and related parts and ammunition.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all firearms and parts and related components exported from the EU to non-EU countries. It does not apply to explosives, detonators, bomb-making equipment or explosive materials.
EU countries must ensure that the export procedures are carried out in accordance with the UN Convention on the Lawful Possession of Firearms and their Parts and Ammunition (COP) and that they comply with the relevant international obligations.
An export authorisation is issued by the competent authorities of the EU country where the exporter is established and must be issued in writing or by electronic means.
The exporter must provide the customs authorities with information on:
the intended end use, consignee, identified final recipient and the risk of diversion;
the name of the consignment and the name and address of the final recipient of the firearms;
a description of the intended end-use and the intended final recipient.
If no export contract has been concluded or if the holder of the contract does not act on its own behalf, the exporters must send the item out of the item to the customs territory of the country where it is intended to be exported.
A customs official may suspend the process of export or, if necessary, otherwise prevent firearms from leaving the EU through that country if they have grounds for suspicion that the reasons substantiated by hunters or sport shooters are not in conformity with relevant considerations and the obligations laid down in Article 10(1) of the COP.
Exports of firearms are subject to the export control procedures laid down by the Cotonou Convention (see summary).
The export controls must be in line with the EU’s export control rules.
Imports are covered by the export controls set out in Regulation (EU) 2017/852 on the control of explosive materials and explosives.
Ammunition is covered by Regulation (Euratom) No 852/2013 on the import control of explosives and detonators.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/853 has applied since 1 July 2018.
BACKGROUND

‘The export control of firearms’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 105:
EUROSUR — situational awareness and reaction capability at the EU’s external borders
EurosURSUR — operational cooperation
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — operational coordination of the European Union Agency for the Protection of the Internal Border and Coastguard (EurOSUR)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a framework for cooperation between EU countries’ border control authorities to improve their situational awareness* and reaction capabilities at the external borders of the EU (‘external borders’) for the purpose of detecting, preventing and combating illegal immigration and cross-border crime and contributing to ensuring the protection and saving the lives of migrants.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries and the European Agency for Law Enforcement Cooperation (Eurojust) in the field of border surveillance.
It does not apply to any legal or administrative measure in the context of operational cooperation coordinated by the Agency.
EU countries and Eurojust must use the EUROSUR framework, consisting of the following components:
national coordination centres;
national situational pictures;
a communication network;
common pre-frontier intelligence picture;
an operational risk analysis report.
National coordination centres
The national coordination centres of EU countries must share with each other, directly and in near-real-time, the situational picture of neighbouring external border sections relating to:
incidents and other significant events contained in the events layer;
tactical risk analysis reports containing in the analysis layer.
common surveillance tools used for collecting information in the communication network
common situational picture
common application of surveillance tools.
The European situational pictures are shared with the European situational picture.
A national coordination centre may refuse a request for technical, financial or operational reasons. The Agency must notify the national coordination center in due time of the reasons for such a refusal.
Cooperation with neighbouring countries
The Agency may cooperate with neighbouring non-EU countries, such as Ireland and the United Kingdom, in order to better achieve the objectives of the Schengen common surveillance picture and common application of the common surveillance tool.
Common application of common surveillance tools
The agency may use on its own initiative the surveillance tools referred to in paragraph 2 for collecting surveillance information which is relevant for the common pre-border intelligence picture and the common situational picture, as well as the common operational risk assessment reports.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Decision No 552/2013/EU has applied since 1 May 2013.
BACKGROUND
EUROOSUR is a common EU strategy to combat illegal immigration. It aims to prevent, detect, combat and combat illegal border crossing and to ensure the protection of people in need of international protection.
For more information, see:
‘Euroesur’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom, Euronews, Euronext, Euroflot) 2019-852 of 1 May 2019 on operational coordination between the European External Action Service (EURosUR) and the Member States of the Union for the Prevention and Control of Illegal Migration and the Interception of Human Trafficking (OJ L 131, 1.5.2019, pp. 1-8)

Summary 106:
Eurodac — automated fingerprinting identification systems
EuroDATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
Regulation (EU) No 604/2013 — Eurodac
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the use of the automated fingerprint identification systems (EurodAC) by the European Union Police Office (Europol) for the prevention, detection or investigation of terrorist offences or of other serious criminal offences.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to EU countries’ designated authorities for law enforcement purposes.
It does not apply to the national authorities of non-EU countries.
EU countries must ensure that their designated authorities have access to the EuroDac Central System, which is used by Europol for the identification of criminal suspects or victims of crime.
The European Commission has adopted a number of implementing acts to implement the regulation, including:
Decision 2009/371/JHA — setting up the European Commission’s European Forensic Identification System (EFS) and Regulation (EU, Euratom) — establishing the European Forensic Identification System (EuroFIS);
Decisions 2008/977/Euratom — establishing EuroFIS and Decision 2008/615/JHHA — establishing a European Forensic Information System for the Identification of Criminal Suspects and Victims of Crime (EurFIS) and Decision 2009/391/EURFIS — establishing an EU Forensic Identities System for Identification of Criminals (EURFS);
Regulations (EC, EC, EC and Euratom — laying down the technical procedures for EuroDAC — setting out the procedures for access to EurofIS and Eurofis;
Commission Regulation (EC) No 552/2014 — setting the procedures to be followed by EU countries for the exchange of data on criminal suspects and victims;
Regulating (EC), EC, EFIS and EurFIS for the protection of personal data — setting procedures for the processing of data;
Delegated acts — setting technical procedures and procedures for data exchange between EU countries and the European Police Agency (Eurofis) — setting rules for EU countries to exchange data on crime victims and criminal suspects, as well as for Eurofists;
Council Decision (EU), EC and EFIS — setting down technical procedures to ensure that EU countries receive unambiguous data by the Eurofisk Central System;
Implementing Decision (EC):
sets out the technical procedure for EurodAC data exchange;
draws up a list of the designated authorities that are authorised to request comparisons with Eurofass;
designates a national authority that is responsible for handling requests for data from the EuroFass Central System.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?

Summary 107:
Protected designations of origin and geographical indications
Protected designs of origin
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — protection of protected designations* of origin, geographical indications and optional quality terms
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the protection of products with a protected designation of origin (DPO) or geographical indication (GID) and the optional quality term (OQS) in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to products originating in a specific place, region or, in exceptional cases, a country and whose quality or characteristics are essentially or exclusively due to a particular geographical environment with its inherent natural and human factors.
It does not apply to products from non-EU countries.
Protection of origin is granted to products that are:
originating in a geographical area situated in another EU country; or
derived from a geographical environment situated in a third country, with the exception of the opposition procedure.
A protected designation of origin or GID must be registered in the EU country where the product originates.
An application for registration of a product must include at least:
the name and address of the applicant group and of the authorities or, if available, the official name of the country of origin;
the production steps of which all take place in the defined geographical area;
proof that the product is protected in that country;
a description of the methods of production;
procedures for the establishment of the production of the product.
the names, symbol and indication must be accompanied by proof that the products are protected in the protected area.
The Commission may adopt implementing acts laying down rules on the form of the specification. These must be adopted in accordance with the regulation’s annexes.
National authorities may refuse to register a product if it does not meet the conditions laid down in the regulation or if it is contrary to national law.
If a national authority refuses to register the product, the product may be subject to an opposition procedure, which allows the applicant to lodge a request for cancellation of the protected designation or the GID. The applicant may also lodge a complaint with the competent national authority.
EU countries may grant transitional protection for up to 10 years, with effect from the date on which either a decision on registration is taken or the application is withdrawn.
Procedure
The European Commission adopts implementing acts on the basis of the annexes to the regulation. These are adopted by national authorities and must be published in the Official Journal of the EU.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
    данскабранка грака  года барка, гъланна варнага карскова,  бъчакога  гша и глаккодна  and ганца манбанда подрацкой горновком гебка are repealed and replaced by Regulation (EC) No 509/2006, enabling them to be registered with reservation of name.
BACKGROUND
* KEY TERMS
* PROTECTED DEPOSITION OF ORIGIN AND GID
* Protected geographical indication: a name which identifies a product as originating in, or derived from, a specific geographical area or a country.
* GID: a geographical indication or a geographical designation that is based on the geographical area of origin of a country or of a region or of an area situated outside the EU, but which is derived from that country or region, and which is essentially, exclusively or in part from that geographical area, or which is in part derived from the geographical environment of that region or a region, or is in whole or part of that area, with inherent natural or human factors;
Optional quality term: a quality term that can be used to indicate that a product is not a product originating in an EU country, but that it is a product derived from an area outside that country, or that it has been produced in a country other than that of that country and/or a region.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Игнодкафралка/гг бодг  кодскка
Council Regulation (Euratom) No 552/2019 of 16 February 2019 on the protection and control of protected designs of origins, geographical indication and optional qualities of products (OJ L 183, 17.2.2019, pp



Summary 108:
Phasing out of older oil tankers — rules on design and registration
Phasing-out of old oil tanker design and registrations
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the phasing out and registration of older single-hull oil tanker designs
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out minimum requirements for the design, registration and operation of oil tanker types in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all oil tanker categories, irrespective of their flag, which enter or leave a port or offshore terminal or anchor in an area under the jurisdiction of an EU country.
It repeals Regulation (Euratom) No 652/2003, which had to be amended by Regulation (EC) No 852/2004 in order to comply with the requirements of the International Maritime Organization (IMO).
It does not apply to vessels that are not in the EU or that are under the flag of a non-EU country, but are registered in another EU country, such as the United Kingdom (1) or the United States of America (1).
EU countries must ensure that the ships comply with all the requirements laid down in the regulation and that they comply with its Annex I to MARPOL 73/78, which sets out the minimum requirements on the design of ships and the registration of vessels.
The EU countries have the right to use delegated acts to prohibit the operation of ships that do not comply with these requirements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECAST APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE APPLY?
 
The new regulation has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission adopted the regulation on behalf of the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Maritime safety’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 109:
European System of Financial Supervision
European system of financial supervision
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/852 establishing the European System of Supervision (ESS)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a European system of supervisory authorities (ESAs) to ensure that EU countries’ financial institutions comply with the rules of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The ESAs are responsible for supervising all financial institutions in the EU.
They are independent and independent from national authorities.
The regulation sets out the tasks of the ESAs and their tasks, including:
provide a centrally accessible database of registered financial institutions;
draw up guidelines and recommendations for financial institutions to take account of the systemic risk posed by them;
assist in preparing equivalence decisions relating to supervisory regimes in non-EU countries;
ensure that EU law is directly applicable to financial institutions by virtue of existing or future EU regulations.
Amendments to the regulation
Amending the regulation amends the regulation to take into account:
the EU’s financial activities protection rules (e.g. rules on the prudential supervision of financial institutions);
the European Banking Authority (EBA) and the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA) rules on capital requirements;
the rules on prudential oversight of banks and other financial institutions.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISION APPLY?
  
It has applied since 1 January 2018.
It had to become law in the following by 1 January 2019.
EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 31 December 2017.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of delegated acts to establish ESAs in the past few years.
For more information, see:
European financial supervisory system (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT

The decision sets out how the ESC is to be set up and how it is to operate.
KEY TERMS
* Supervisory authority: an authority responsible for the supervision of a financial institution by national authorities in an EU country.
* Financial activities protection: the protection of the financial system against the risk of a bank or other financial institution failing to comply with EU law.

Summary 110:
Freedom of movement
Freedom of mobility
SUMMigration
The right of all workers in the EU to pursue the activity of their choice within the EU should be affirmed.
ACT
Council Regulation (EU) No 552/2011 of 21 March 2011 on the right of workers to pursue their activity of choice within their EU countries
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force - Date of expiry
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 550/2011
-
OJ L 183 of 21.3.2011
Settlement of workers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It aims to ensure that all workers who wish to work in another EU country have the same rights and benefits as nationals of the EU country in which they live and work.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 852/2010, which had been amended several times.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all workers, permanent, seasonal and frontier workers, as well as those who pursue their activities for the purpose of providing services.
Nationals of one EU country may not be excluded from taking part in the management of bodies governed by public law and from holding an office governed by the public law of another country.
Eligibility for employment
The following criteria are used to determine eligibility for employment:
nationals must meet the following criteria:
medical, vocational or other criteria which are not discriminatory on grounds of nationality by comparison with those applied to nationals of other EU countries;
they must not depend on medical or vocational qualifications;
the applicant must not be a national of a non-EU country;
their qualifications must be equivalent to those of nationals of an EU country who are employed in the territory of the other EU country for the same activity.
The specialist services of each EU country must forward to the services of the first EU country the details of suitable applications.
EU countries must send to the specialist services and the European Coordination Office the following information concerning living and working conditions and the state of the labour market as likely to be of guidance to workers from the other countries:
details of vacancies which could be filled by nationals of non-euro area workers;
information of applications for employment by those who have formally expressed a wish to apply for employment in another country; and
information, by region and by branch of activity, on applicants who have declared themselves actually willing to accept employment.
An Advisory Committee composed of representatives of EU countries, the European Commission and the Technical Committee is responsible for advising the Council on the implementation of the regulation.
Amendments to Regulation (Euratom) 2018/852
Amending Decision (EU), Euratom No 553/2011 has been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The legislation entered into force on 22 March 2011 and had to become law in the European Union countries by 22 March 2012.
BACKGROUND
Equal treatment for workers
For more information, see:
Equality of treatment for EU workers (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* National: a person whose nationality is determined by the laws or regulations of the country where he or she lives or works.
* Frontier worker: a worker who is employed outside the EU but who has the same social and tax advantages as national workers in matters of housing, including ownership of the housing he needs.
Employment: an activity for which a person has the right to work, but who is not entitled to the same benefits as a national worker.
MAIN DOCUMENT
