Summary 145:
Benefits in respect of accidents at work and occupational diseases — EU countries’ rules on access to social security benefits
Benefits at work or in the event of residence or stay in a Member State other than the one in which the person is resident
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 883/2004 on the access to benefits in the Member States of the European Union (EU)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the application of EU social security legislation in Member States.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU citizens who are entitled to benefit in kind and in cash from the social security system in an EU country other than their country of residence.
It does not apply to:
people who are unemployed or who have been unemployed for more than 6 months;
persons who have left the EU for a period of more than 2 years;
people with disabilities who have not been able to work for at least 6 months.
Beneficiaries
The legislation applies to the following types of benefits:
benefits in kind:
the benefits in kind provided by the EU country where the claimant lives and works are reimbursed by the institutions providing those benefits, on the basis of a fixed amount established for each calendar year;
the cash benefits provided in the country of the claimant’s place of residence;
beneficiaries’ contributions to the national social security fund (NSF):
the amount paid by the institution providing the cash benefits and the amount of the institution reimbursing that institution for the period of the person has been unemployed or staying in another EU country;
benefit in kind of social security in the institution is reimbursed to the institution which provides the cash benefit.
Provisional calculation of benefits and contributions
The European Commission must lay down implementing measures for this regulation where necessary.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?

Summary 146:
Statistics on public health and health and safety at work — comparable statistics and indicators
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1350/2007/EC on the collection of comparable data and information on the European Commission’s statistical activities in the field of public health
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the minimum statistical data set needed for the calculation of the European Health and Safety at Work (ECHI) indicator.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all deaths and stillbirths occurring in each EU country, distinguishing residents and non-residents.
The data are collected by the Commission (Eurostat) in cooperation with the United Nations and its special organisations, such as the World Health Organisation (WHO) and the International Labour Organisation (ILO), as well as the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD), when relevant and possible.
EU countries must transmit the data and metadata required by this regulation in electronic form, in accordance with an interchange standard agreed between the Commission and the EU countries.
Data collection
The Commission collects the data on the following areas:
deaths
stillbirths
public health
health at work
the number of deaths and deaths caused by occupational accidents
the total number of people who die or are stillborn in the EU each year.
Eurostat collects data on these areas through administrative sources.
National authorities must ensure that the data are compiled on a voluntary basis and that they are collected in a minimum of 5 years before the end of each calendar year. The data must be collected by EU countries’ national authorities.
In order to ensure relevance and comparability of the data, national authorities must collect data on:
the characteristics of the population covered by the data;
the causes of death and the number of stillborns;
health and safety conditions at work; and
the quality of health care at work.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The legislation has applied since 1 January 2008. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
   
The European Commission is responsible for collecting and disseminating statistics on health at work in the European Union (EU).
For more information, see:
Health at work (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Deaths: deaths that occur in the course of the work day.
* Stillbirths: deaths resulting from the birth of a child under the age of 28 days.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU) No 1305/2007 of 23 October 2007 establishing a second programme of Community action in the area of health (2008-2013)

Summary 147:
Statistics on job vacancies — quarterly production of EU data on employment vacancies
Statistics on jobs vacancies — yearly production of European Union (EU) data
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 322/97 on the production of statistics on Community job vacancies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the requirements for EU countries to produce statistics on EU job vacancies.
It aims to improve the understanding of the EU’s employment situation and prospects, in particular through analysis and studies and the development of statistics and common indicators within the framework of the European Employment Strategy (see summary).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries.
EU countries must provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with data on the number of job vacancies in the EU each quarter.
The data must be broken down by economic activity in accordance with the NACE in force at section level.
Data must be transmitted to Eurostat by the end of the first reference quarter and the breakdowns no later than 1 year after the first data transmission.
National sample schemes may be established and coordinated by Eurostat in order to produce Community estimates where national sample schemes do not meet the EU requirements with regard to quarterly data collection.
Eurostat must transmit the data using business surveys.
Each EU country must send the data to the Commission within 3 months of receiving the data. The Commission must assess the quality of the data transmitted and send a report to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee on the implementation of the regulation within 3 years after receiving the results of the feasibility studies on the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLYEARLY ENTRY INTO FORCELEBRATION

This regulation applies from 1 January 2007.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:

KEY TERMS
* Employment vacancies: job vacancies are defined in the European Central Statistical System (ESS).
* Business surveys: surveys conducted by EU countries on the economic activities of households as employers and the activities of extraterritorial organisations and bodies.
* NACE: the network of national statistics on economic activity (NACE) in force in the Member States.

Summary 148:
Safety of hydrogen-powered vehicles — type-approval of hydrogen systems and their components in the EU (Regulation (EC) No 552/2014)
Safety of the hydrogen system and its components in EU cars
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/40/EU — type approval of hydrogen vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
  
It sets out the requirements for the type of hydrogen* systems* and components* that must be installed in motor vehicles in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
vehicles designed to use compressed (gaseous) hydrogen with a nominal working pressure of over 3.0 MPa;
hydrogen containers designed to contain liquid hydrogen that contains the cryogenic hydrogen.
It does not apply to hydrogen systems designed for use in stationary stationary power stations.
Manufacturers must provide information for the purposes of inspection of hydrogen components and systems during the service life of the vehicle.
The test procedures for hydrogen containers must include:
Burst test: the purpose of the test is to provide evidence that the hydrogen container does not fail before a specified level of high pressure, the burst pressure (safety factor multiplied by the maximum filling level test (MAWP) is exceeded.
Pressure test: a specific number of test cycles must be carried out for the hydrogen component under specified temperature and pressure conditions.
Leak test: an external leakage test is carried out to check that the container is not leaking.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE APPLY?
It entered into force on 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
 
The EU has a comprehensive type approval system for motor vehicles.
For more information, see:
‘Hydrogen vehicles’ on the European Commission’s website
* KEY TERMS
* Hydrogen systems and components in a motor vehicle: components that contain hydrogen that contain cryogenic (non-metallic) hydrogen and are designed to operate at a temperature of -40°C and a pressure of -50°C.

Summary 149:
Network codes for access to the internal market in natural gas — common rules for natural gas transmission networks
Network codes on access to natural gas distribution networks — Common rules for access and pricing
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1775/2005 on conditions for accessing and managing effective and transparent network codes for providing and managing access to EU natural gas networks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down basic rules for the operation of the European Union’s (EU) natural gas (natural gas) transmission networks.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all gas transmission systems in the EU. It does not apply to pipelines.
It sets out the rules for:
access to the networks of transmission system operators;
tariffs for network access;
regional cooperation;
information on the network codes;
transmission system operators’ network management procedures;
the rules for congestion management;
rules for interconnecting pipelines and pipelines;
network users’ rights to re-sell or sublet their unused contracted capacity on the secondary market.
Decision 2009/73/EC on network codes
The European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas (ENTSO for Gas) is responsible for developing and implementing network codes. It is assisted by the European Commission and the Agency for Energy Regulation (Euratom).
It is assisted in this process by the Euratom, the European Gas Network Operators’ Association (EGN) and the European Transmission System Operator Network Coordination Network (ETN) for Gas.
EU countries.
FROMISSION
The ENTSO has the power to adopt network codes on its own initiative.
The rules for network codes are set out in the regulation.
Network operators must operate their networks in accordance with those network codes in line with those codes.
They must:
provide information on the status and efficiency of the system;
ensure that the information they provide is accurate, transparent and up-to-date;
make available to the public all the information necessary to assess the overall demand and supply situation and to identify the reasons for movements in the wholesale price.
Regional cooperation
The EGNs must cooperate at regional level to ensure that their networks operate smoothly and efficiently. They must also cooperate at national level to improve the efficiency of their networks and to ensure the smooth operation of their pipelines, pipelines and interconnections.
In addition, they must cooperate with each other in order to:
avoid cross-subsidisation between network users and not hamper the entry of new market entrants;
coordinate their network operations;
share information on their networks;
monitor the performance of their systems;
cooperate with other market participants;
take corrective action in the event of technical or operational problems;
inform the Commission of any planned or actual disruptions affecting the network;
report to the Commission on any maintenance or supply interruption affecting the system.
National authorities must ensure that:
information is made available to all market participants, including the public, on the availability of the network code;
all network users have the right to access the network and to make use of the information provided by the transmission system operator;
national authorities must provide the Commission with all the necessary information to determine the impact of any maintenance, supply or transit interruption on the system and on other network users;
any maintenance or transit disruption must be notified to the national authorities of the affected areas and to the EGN operators.
A network code must be adopted within 3 years of the date on which it is adopted by the national authority in question.
If a national authority fails to adopt a network code within the 3-year deadline set by the Commission, the Commission may request the Agency to prepare a draft network code on the basis of the relevant framework guideline. The Agency may launch a further consultation in the course of preparing a draft code. The Commission may also propose amendments to any network code adopted under the framework guideline if it considers that the draft code does not meet the requirements of the regulation or that it does not comply with the principles set out above.
An amendment to the regulation must be submitted to the European Parliament, the Council or the European Economic and Social Committee (EEC) by the end of the 3 years following the adoption of the new network code. If the Commission considers that an amendment has not been submitted, it must inform the Agency of its decision and inform the other parties involved in the consultation process of its reasons for its decision.

Summary 150:
Judicial cooperation in civil matters between EU countries and non-EU countries
Juditable cooperation within the European Union (EU) — judicial cooperation between EU states and third countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on judicial cooperation
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out procedures for EU countries to obtain an authorisation from the European Commission to open or continue formal negotiations on an agreement with a third country on the same subject matter as an existing agreement with an EU country.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU countries that have concluded an agreement or are in the process of concluding an agreement on civil matters relating to civil matters with a non-European Union country (non-EU country).
EU countries must notify the Commission of ongoing or already announced negotiations with a view to obtaining authorisation to open formal negotiations or to conclude an agreement.
Notification to the Commission
The Commission must send a report to the European Parliament and to the Council within 30 days of receiving the notification.
The report must contain information on:
the nature and scope of the agreement;
the EU country concerned’s position on the agreement,
the conditions for authorising it to conclude the agreement and
the reasons for refusing to do so.
If the Commission considers that the agreement meets the conditions set out in the regulation, it must authorise the EU country to conclude it or to amend the agreement or to replace it with a subsequent agreement. If it considers that an agreement does not meet these conditions, it may refuse to authorise it or amend it.
FROMENTRY INTO FORCE
The notification must be sent by the Commission within 90 days of receipt of the notification, or within 130 days after receiving it. The Commission must then give a reasoned decision on the application of the regulation to conclude or amend the negotiated agreement. The decision must be published in the Official Journal of the European Community.
Authorisation to conclude a negotiated agreement
The agreement must be concluded by the EU countries concerned within 30 working days of the Commission giving its opinion on whether or not it is in the interest of the EU or not. If the agreement is not concluded, the Commission must give its opinion to the Member State concerned, as well as to the EU Parliament and the Council, within 60 days of its decision.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force - Date of expiry
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Decision 2009/552/EC
29.7.2009
-
OJ L 347 of 29.7-30.09
Amending the agreement
Amendments to the agreement are subject to the same conditions as those laid down in Article 8(2) of the original agreement. However, the amendments may not be identical to those contained in the initial agreement, as they are not binding on the other parties.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
‘Judicial Cooperation in Civil Matters’ on the Commission's website.

Regulation (EC) No 343/2003 on the collection and analysis of Community Statistics in the field of migration
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for the collection, analysis and transmission of EU statistics on the EU’s migration statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope

information on illegal entry and stay.

Summary 152:
Statutory audits of public-sector companies
Statutory audits of public sector companies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1092/2010 on the appointment of statutory auditors and audit firms
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the selection of statutory audit* and audit firm* professionals to carry out the statutory audit of publicly-listed companies in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries that have a statutory auditor or an audit firm responsible for the public-interest audit of their companies.
It does not apply to companies that have not been audited by an EU country’s competent authorities or bodies, such as the European Systemic Risk Board (ESRB) or the European Audit Office (EAAO).
It applies to:
public-sector entities with a turnover of more than €1 billion;
companies that have more than 1,000 employees;
financial institutions with more than 500 employees.
EU countries may decide to delegate the tasks referred to in the regulation to other EU countries or bodies designated or otherwise authorised by law, when the majority of the persons involved in the governance of the authority or body concerned is independent from the audit profession.
The EU countries must ensure that:
the selection procedure is transparent and non-discriminatory;
the audit committee is independent of the audit firms;
there are no conflicts of interest between the audit committee and the statutory auditor and the audit firm.
A statutory audit or audit firm may not provide non-audit services which are not covered by the regulation if they do not pose a threat to the independence of the auditor.
An audit report must be in clear and unambiguous language.
Auditors must be independent from any other person or body that is responsible for performing the audit of the same entity.
Eligibility of statutory audits
The European Commission must publish the names of the competent authorities that have been designated by EU countries for the purpose of applying the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2011/33/EU has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The statutory audit is one of the main tasks of the European systemic risk board and the EAAO.
For more information, see:
‘Statutory audit’ on the European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Statutory audit: an independent audit of a public sector company.
* Audit firm: a company that provides independent audit services.
ACT

Summary 153:
Conservation of marine biological resources in the Mediterranean Sea
Conservation and management of marine biodiversity
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 — Common Fisheries Policy for the period 2014-2020
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the conservation of marine living resources and the management of fisheries targeting them.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the EU’s common fisheries policy (CFP), which aims to conserve and manage the marine life of the Mediterranean and the Atlantic oceans.
The CFP is the main instrument of the EU fisheries policy.
It aims to:
promote the sustainable exploitation of marine life;
ensure that the best available scientific advice is taken into account in the decision-making process;
protect and manage marine ecosystems;
encourage the sustainable use of the marine environment;
improve the protection of marine species;
reduce the impact of overfishing on marine ecosystems.
EU countries must submit to the European Commission, the information they have collected and the data they have provided to the Advisory Councils on the conservation and management measures they have adopted to achieve the objectives of the CFP.
Each year, the Commission adopts a multiannual marine management plan (MMP) which sets out the conservation objectives and measures that are necessary to achieve them. The MMP must be adopted by the end-users in accordance with the objectives set out in the MMP.
FROMMMPs
The MMPs may contain specific conservation objectives or measures based on the ecosystem approach in order to address the specific problems of mixed fisheries in relation to the achievement of the objectives.
An Advisory Council is set up to advise the Commission on the implementation of MMPAs and to provide the Commission with scientific advice on the measures to be adopted.
A Commission report is sent to the Council and the European Parliament, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee for fisheries and aquaculture every 2 years. The Commission is assisted by a committee within the meaning of Regulation (EC) No 182/2011.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
  
The legislation entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Maritime and fisheries policy’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 154:
Common organisation of the markets in fishery and aquaculture products (CMO)
Common operation of the common markets in fisheries and aqua-products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 establishing a common organisation of markets in fish and shellfish
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up the Common Organisation of the Markets in Fishery and Aquaculture Products, the CMO, which aims to improve the conditions for the placing on the market of products from EU countries’ fishery or aquacultural industries.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The CMO is an integral part of the Common Fisheries Policy (CFP) and is designed to contribute to the stabilisation and convergence of local markets in the EU with a view to achieving the objectives of the internal market.
It aims to:
facilitate the movement of products between EU countries;
improve the quality, size, weight, packing, presentation or labelling of products;
ensure that products are marketed in a more efficient and sustainable manner;
increase the level of competition to the production of, and trade in, agricultural products.
The regulation sets out the responsibilities of the producer organisations (known as associations of producer organisations) which have been recognised by the European Commission and the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) for the production and marketing of fish, shellfish and fish.
Objectives
The objective of the association of producers is to achieve the following objectives:
to:
promote the production, packaging, packaging and presentation of products in a way that meets the objectives;
to improve the quality of the products and to ensure that they are labelled in accordance with the standards set out in Regulation (EC) No 853/2004 on animal health and hygiene rules for food of food of origin (see summary);
to ensure that the products are labelled according to the standards laid down in the regulation;
provide consumers with information on the products they buy and the conditions under which they can buy them.
Associations of producers
The associations of producers may pursue the objectives listed above by:
improving the quality and packaging of their members’ products, taking into account the best available scientific advice;
promoting the sustainable management of their member producer organisations’ activities;
coordinating and developing activities of common interest for the member producers organisations.
Member producer organisations may also pursue two or more of the objectives set out above, in addition to the objectives laid down above:
improveing the conditions to be placed on the markets for their members' fishery products, in particular by setting minimum marketing sizes corresponding, where relevant, to minimum conservation reference sizes;
specifications of preserved products in line with conservation requirements and international obligations;
establishing a common storage mechanism to store fish stocks until such stocks have been used up.
Authorisation
Member countries may grant or withdraw the recognition of an association if it fails to fulfil its objectives or if it does not comply with the requirements of the regulation.
A producer organisation may apply for an authorisation from an EU country that does not recognise it.
An association may be established at the initiative of a producer organisation recognised in one or more EU countries and may be bound by the provisions of this regulation and to comply with its provisions.
If an association is recognised in more than one EU country, it must submit to the Commission an application for the authorisation to be granted by the EU country in which it is based. The Commission then forwards the application to the other EU countries, which then forwards it to the EFSA, which forwards it back to the EU countries that have granted or withdrawn the recognition to the producer organisation in question.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?

SUMMARY OF:
Regulation 2014/65/EU on post-trader services (CSDs)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for providing securities settlement services* for issuers in the EU and non-EU countries.

KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
post-traded services* provided by CSDs;
non-banking-type services provided by a credit institution designated by the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA).

EU countries must ensure that CSDs comply with the requirements of the regulation by 18 June 2015.
The CSDs must be authorised by the competent national authorities.
A CSD must have the necessary authorisation to provide PSD-type PSD services.
An application for PSD authorisation must be submitted to the competent authority within 3 months of receiving it.

Summary 156:
Cohesion Fund for the transport and energy sectors
Cohesion fund for the transportation and energy sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 establishing the European Union’s Cohesion Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) and the European Investment Bank (EIB).
It aims to provide financial support to projects in the fields of environment and trans-European networks in the area of transport infrastructure.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EIB is the main instrument of the EU's cohesion policy, which aims to reduce greenhouse gas emissions (GHG emissions) in the EU.
The regulation sets out how the EIB and EIB are to be used for this purpose.
It is the first of a series of EU-wide measures to establish a European Union (EU)-wide fund to support investment in the areas of environment, energy, transport infrastructure and transport.
Eligibility
EU countries are eligible for EIB support if they have:
investment in the environment, including areas related to sustainable development and energy which present environmental benefits;
transport infrastructure, including projects related to the development of sustainable development, energy and transport;
major projects, including major projects, in the field of transport, in order to achieve the reduction of GHG emissions from activities listed in Annex I to Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council (see summary);
transmission of goods and services, such as rail, roadways, airports, ports, seaports, railways, airports and other forms of transport in the European Economic Area of Transport (EEA), in the EEA, in accordance with Regulation (EC) No 1315/2013;
technical assistance.
Projects that are part of operational programmes and major projects are excluded from the scope of EIB.
Funds may not be used to finance projects that do not meet the objectives of the investment priorities set out in the thematic objectives.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
  
The Regulation applies from 21 December 2013 until 31 December 2020.

Summary 157:
European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) — framework for the European territorial cooperation goal (2013-2020)
European Regional development fund (2013 - 2020)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 on the European Regional Development Facility
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the EU’s regional development fund and the European Territorial Cooperation goal (Euratom).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The ERDF is the main instrument of the European Union (EU), which aims to contribute to reducing disparities between the levels of development of the various regions and to reducing the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to regions which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.
The regulation lays down the type of activities which can be supported by the ERDF, in order to support the investment priorities within the thematic objectives set out in Article 174 TFEU of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU (TFEU).
The objectives of the Euratom are to:
increase the level of development in the most deprived regions;
reduce disparities between regions and the most developed regions and regions which are least developed;
improve the quality of life in the least developed regions, particularly in terms of health, education, housing and social services;
promote sustainable urban development;
contribute to the creation of jobs and growth and jobs;
support the development of cities and towns;
encourage innovation in urban areas;
provide financial support for projects that address issues that are relevant at EU level.
Scope of support
The EURDF is designed to support activities in the following areas:
investment in the investment for growth, jobs and jobs goal;
investments in the Investment for jobs goal.
In order to achieve these objectives, the EURRDF is to support innovative actions in the area of urban development.
It is also responsible for:
supporting the implementation of integrated actions for sustainable urban developments (i.e. projects that aim to improve urban areas’ capacity to develop sustainable urban areas and reduce their environmental impact;
facilitating the sharing of facilities and human resources, and all types of infrastructure across borders in all regions. The EURD supports innovative actions which address issues related to sustainable cities and new solutions that are of relevance at Union level, such as:
the creation of a network of urban areas to support integrated urban development initiatives;
the development of a sustainable urban area network to improve the quality and efficiency of urban transport;
improving the efficiency of the transport sector;
developing a sustainable transport network to reduce emissions of greenhouse gas emissions from activities listed in Annex I to Directive 2003/87/EC (see summary).
In addition to the above-mentioned activities, EURDP may also support the following activities:
promoting risk management investments, in particular by:
encouraging risk-based risk management;
ensuring that the EERDF is not used to finance activities that are contrary to the objectives of Horizon 2020;
fostering innovation;
establishing a European urban development network;
enhancing the capacity of cities, towns, villages and cities to develop innovative urban development solutions;
creating an integrated urban environment;
increasing the number of jobs in cities;
strengthening the competitiveness of the labour market.
EURDP is also able to provide financial support to projects that are complementary to those undertaken under Horizon 2020.

Summary 158:
European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) — the European territorial cooperation goal
European regional development fund (Euratom) – the European regional development goal
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 establishing the scope of the European Regional Development fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the EU’s framework for implementing the European Territorial Cooperation goal and lays down specific provisions concerning that goal.
It aims to contribute to reducing disparities between the levels of development of the various regions and to reducing the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to rural areas, areas affected by industrial transition, and regions which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation sets out the scope and priorities of the ERDF for the 2007-2013 programming period (2007-2013) and for the 2014-2020 period (2014-2020).
Funding
The ERDF is funded by the European Structural and Investment Funds (ESIF) and the European Investment Bank (EIB).
It is the main instrument of the EU's cohesion policy, which aims to support the development of Europe's regions and the least developed regions. It is also the main source of financial support for the European Union's (EU's) cohesion policy.
The programme is divided into 3 strands:
Interregional cooperation — the aim to improve the quality of life for the most deprived regions and regions in the EU, particularly in rural areas and the most disadvantaged regions, in particular in the north, south and east;
interregional development — aims to increase the level of development in the least deprived regions, especially in the south, east and west;
integrated territorial investment — aims at improving the quality and efficiency of investment in the regions and areas most deprived by industrialisation and the social exclusion of rural areas.
Cooperation programmes — the programme designates regions, areas and areas that are eligible for support from the EIF and the EIB for the 2013-2020 programming period.
Programmes — the EDF and EIB are divided into 4 strands.
Scope of funding
The EDF covers the entire territory of the Union and all NUTS level 3 regions of the union along maritime borders separated by a maximum of 150 km, without prejudice to potential adjustments needed to ensure the coherence and continuity of cooperation programme areas established for the 2017-2020 programme period. The EDF also supports regional development projects in the North, the south and the east.
Objective criteria for designating eligible regions
The objective criteria are set out in the regulation. They include:
the geographical concentration and investment priorities;
the thematic concentration of the programmes;
a list of major projects for which the implementation is planned during the programming period;
an evaluation plan for each of the projects.
Eligible regions are defined according to the geographical concentration of their respective programmes and the investment priorities set out by the programme authorities.
A steering committee composed of representatives of the beneficiaries, programme authorities, authorities in participating EU countries, at local, regional or national level, as appropriate, and third countries, as well as the Commission, is responsible for managing the programme and the steering committee is chaired by the managing authority.
An EGTC is set up under the laws of one of the participating countries provided that it has been set up by at least two public authorities or bodies from at least 2 participating countries, and that it is composed of at least one public authority or body from each participating country. The managing authority is assisted by a legal body established under the law of a participating country or by an auditing body.
EU countries are responsible for the management and implementation of the cooperation programmes.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 30 June 2013 and had to become law in the Member States by 30 June 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
 * Regional development goal: the goal of the Energies for Europe goal is to reduce disparities between levels of growth and to reduce the disadvantage of regions and in particular the least disadvantaged regions in terms of their level of economic development.
* European territorial development goal (EURD): the goal is achieved by improving the conditions for regional development in order to reduce social exclusion and social exclusion in the various areas of the region.

Summary 159:
Smart grids: smart energy infrastructure
Smart energy infrastructure: smart electricity infrastructure
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on smart grids
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for smart grids in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to projects in the energy infrastructure categories of electricity and gas.
It does not apply to projects of common interest (i.e. projects that are not part of the EU’s energy policy objectives).
It applies to all energy infrastructure projects, whether they are in the electricity or gas sectors.
Decision No 553/2013/EU sets out a procedure for granting permits for smart grid projects in order to ensure that they comply with the regulation.
Projects must meet the following criteria:
have a net positive impact on the energy system wide cost-benefit analysis;
have an impact on market integration and interoperability;
provide a high level of security of supply and demand.
The project promoter must draw up and submit a concept for public participation to the competent authority, following the process outlined in the manual referred to in Article 10(1)(a) of the regulation, in line with the guidelines set out in Annex VI.
A decision to grant a permit must be published in the Official Journal of the European Atomic Energy Community (OJ C 202 of the EEC.
Implementation and monitoring of smart grids must be monitored by the competent authorities in the EU countries.
EU countries must ensure that the projects are implemented and that they have designated competent authorities are operational as soon as possible.
If a project does not meet the criteria listed in the regulation is deemed to be a common interest, the European Commission, the EEA and the European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas (ENTSO) may issue a decision to revoke the permit.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 30 September 2013 and had to become law in all EU countries by 30 September 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to encourage investment in smart grids.
For more information, see:
‘Smart grids’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Smart grid: a network of interconnected energy infrastructure, such as energy storage, transmission, distribution and distribution networks, that can be used to provide electricity, gas and/or other energy-related services to consumers, businesses and the public.

Summary 160:
Alternative dispute resolution (ADR) for online sales and service contracts — online dispute resolution
Alternative challenge resolution (ODR)*
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — alternative dispute resolution for online sale and service contract disputes
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out rules for the use of the online dispute redress system (ODR) platform for disputes arising from online sales or service contracts.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the out-of-court resolution of disputes initiated by a trader against a consumer, in so far as the legislation of the EU country where the consumer is habitually resident allows for such disputes to be resolved through the intervention of an ADR entity.
The ODR platform is an interactive website which can be accessed electronically and free of charge in all the official languages of the institutions of the European Union (EU).
It provides an electronic complaint form to be filled in by the complainant party in accordance with Directive 2013/11/EU (see summary).
Disputes can be resolved by an ODR entity if:
the trader refuses to deal with the dispute;
the complainant party does not have the necessary information to resolve the dispute in a timely manner;
an ODR contact point is located in a non-EU country;
a dispute has not been resolved by the trader.
An ODR agreement is entered into by the consumer in the ODR database and stored in the database.
ADR entities to which have been registered with the platform are obliged to use the case management tool to resolve disputes.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY TO APPLY?
Directive 2013/12/2013/EU sets out the rules for implementing the regulation.
Decision 2013/13/EU was adopted by the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee.
BACKGROUND
The EU’s digital single market is one of the 12 levers to boost growth and strengthen confidence in the single market.
For more information, see:
‘Alternative Dispute Resolution for Online Sales and Service Contracts’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Alternative dispute resolution: a dispute resolution procedure where a dispute is brought by a consumer against a trader for the sale or service of a product or service.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/853 of 12 April 2018 on alternative dispute resolutions for online selling and service contractual disputes (codified version)
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Commission Delegated Decision 2014/856/EU on the implementation of Regulation 2013/23/EU establishing the electronic dispute resolution mechanism for online marketplaces and repealing Decision 2004/387/EC

Summary 161:
Single payment scheme for the Common Agricultural Policy (CAP) for the period 2014-2020 (reform)
Single payment system for the common agricultural policy (reformation)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1306/2013 on the European Union’s common Agricultural Policy
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the implementation of the common agriculture policy (CAP).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland.
It applies to the EU countries that have not yet adopted a national reserve.
EU countries must apply the single payment scheme at national level.
The basic payment scheme is based on the principle of a minimum level of support for each hectare of arable land.
Croatia is one of the countries that has not yet applied the basic payment system.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The new regulation entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Union has been implementing the Common Agriculture Policy for the past 4 years.
For more information, see:
‘Common Agricultural Policy’ on the EU's website.
KEY TERMS
* Common Agricultural Programme (CAP): a system of support to farmers for the production of crops, livestock, forestry, fisheries and aquaculture.

Summary 162:
Agricultural support programme for the smaller Aegean islands (Aegean Regional Development Mechanism) (2006-2013) (see summary)
Agriculture Support Programme for the small and medium-sized islands (EaRMs) (2007-2013). See summary
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006/2006 on the European Agricultural Support Mechanism for the Small and Medium-sized Islands of the Eastern Mediterranean (AaRMS)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the conditions for the European Union (EU) to provide financial support to the smaller islands of the eastern Mediterranean and the western Mediterranean for the development of their agricultural production.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to measures that Greece has implemented under the EU’s regional development mechanism for the eastern and western Mediterranean, known as the AeG programme.
The programme is an essential tool for supplying those islands with agricultural products and for supporting local agricultural production, as well as for the preservation and development of local agriculture.
It aims to:
promote the sustainable development of agricultural production on the islands;
improve the supply of agricultural products;
encourage the production of quality products, and the marketing of such products in the region;
ensure that the islands’ farmers have access to quality products and that they are supplied with sufficient quantities to meet their needs;
support the production and processing of raw and processed agricultural products in accordance with the requirements of the local market;
provide technical assistance to farmers;
inform the European Commission of the conditions under which the aid is to be used;
contribute to the implementation of the regional development strategy;
facilitate the exchange of information between the EU and the islands.
Specific supply arrangements
The European Commission may adopt delegated acts to authorise specific supply arrangements for specific agricultural products.
EU countries must notify the Commission of any measures that are part of the support programme and the amount of aid to be provided for.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULICITY APPLY?
Decision 2006/53/EC has applied since 1 July 2006.
BACKGROUND
   
The AaRms programme is part of a package of measures designed to support the economic development of the smaller and mid-sized eastern Mediterranean islands and the Western Mediterranean.
For more information, see:
AeG support programme (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Agricultural support programme: the programme provides financial support for the production, processing and marketing of agricultural and processing products in order to encourage the development and supply of quality agricultural products, in particular for the sustainable production and distribution of raw products, for the exploitation of the natural resources of the region in which they are produced, and for the marketing and transport of processed products outside the region.
* Regional development Mechanism: a European Union programme designed to promote regional development, including the creation of a regional development framework for the western and eastern Mediterranean, and to provide technical assistance for farmers, traders and other interested parties.

SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2013 on the collection of EU country-level statistics on the road transport of goods
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection and transmission of national road transport data by EU countries to Eurostat, the European statistical office responsible for compiling official statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all road transport operations in the European Union (EU) by means of a combination of road transport vehicles, namely road train or articulated vehicle, in which the goods road transport vehicle and the trailer or semi-trailer are registered in different EU countries.

Summary 164:
Transmission and service of judicial documents between EU countries in civil and commercial matters (Article 3) of the Hague Convention on the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia
Telecommunication and communication of documents relating to judicial cooperation in civil matters (EC) No 1348/2000
Telecommunications and communication between EU governments
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2015/849 on the European Judicial Network in Civil and Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve and expedite the transmission and the service of legal documents between the EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation lays down the rules for the establishment of an area of judicial cooperation for the purposes of the European Union (EU).
It establishes a common European system for the transmission of judicial and commercial documents.
EU countries must designate a central body responsible for:
supplying information to the transmitting agencies;
seeking solutions to any difficulties which may arise during transmission of documents for service;
forwarding, in exceptional cases, a request for service to the competent receiving agency.
Each EU country must designate one transmitting agency and one receiving agency, or one agency to perform both functions, for a period of 5 years.
The central body may designate more than one such agency, depending on the nature of the legal system or the type of legal system.
A transmitting agency may also designate one or more agencies to carry out the following tasks:
transmitting judicial documents to the receiving agencies for the purpose;
providing information on the conditions of service, in the event that the transmitting agency is unable to do so;
delivering a document to a receiving agency;
making a request to a transmitting agency for service.
Transmitting and receiving agencies must notify the central body of any information or documents that are missing or have been lost or destroyed.
If a document is missing or destroyed or has been refused to be served, the receiving agency must provide the information and documents it has received to the transmitted agency by the deadline specified in the regulation’s annexes.
When a document has been lost, the agency responsible for providing the information must provide a certificate of service and a copy of the document to the requesting agency, which must be sent to the agency that provided the information.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULATION APPLY?
Regulation (EU, Euratom and EU countries must apply it from 1 June 2015.
It has applied since 1 June 2011.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to ensure the proper functioning of the internal market.
For more information, see:
European judicial cooperation (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Judicial cooperation: the cooperation of EU countries’ courts, tribunals, administrative and judicial authorities in civil or commercial matters.
* Telecommunication: the exchange of information and communication by means of electronic means.

Summary 165:
EU rules for advanced therapy medicinal products — new medicines for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body (Regulation (EC) No 726/2004 on advanced therapy medicines for human use (see amending acts)
EU rules on advanced therapies for the use of human tissues and cells
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — EU rules on the marketing of advanced therapy therapeutic products for human uses
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the marketing and evaluation of advanced therapies* for diseases and disorders caused by cells, tissues or other biological substances.
It aims to improve the quality of clinical trials for new medicines in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all new medicines that have the potential to treat human diseases or disorders. It does not apply to existing medicines.
Manufacturers must submit a marketing application to the European Medicines Agency (EMA) for authorisation of their products.
The application must include a description of the physical characteristics and performance of the product and the product design methods, in accordance with Annex I to Directive 2001/83/EC.
Annex II to the regulation sets out the labelling of the products and the information to be provided by the manufacturer.
EU countries must inform the European Commission of any adverse reactions or reactions that may occur in relation to an advanced therapy product.
Evaluation procedure
An EU country’s competent authorities must carry out a scientific evaluation of the medicinal product before authorising it to be marketed in the EU.
A European Commission committee for advanced therapies is responsible for evaluating and certifying the medicinal products. The committee is composed of experts in the field of biomedicine and is chaired by the Commission.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 July 2017.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Advanced therapy medicinal product: a medicine that uses cells or tissues to treat a disease or disorder.
* Combination therapy: a treatment that combines a drug with a medical device to treat the disease or disease.

EU type of approval requirements for fuels and exhaust gases from motor vehicles
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 12/2013/2013 on the type approval system for motor vehicles and their trailers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the EU type approval procedure for motor cars and light commercial vehicles.
It aims to reduce the emissions of greenhouse gases (GHGs) emitted by motor vehicles by reducing their fuel consumption.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to motor vehicles with a gross tonnage of more than 10,000 kg and a total fuel consumption of over 1,500 kg.
EU countries must apply the type approvals system for these vehicles in accordance with the EU’s national legislation.
Manufacturers are required to submit information on their vehicles’ fuel consumption, exhaust emissions and CO2 emissions to the European Commission, which then forwards the information to the EU countries’ competent authorities.
Vehicle manufacturers must submit the information in a standardised format, known as the OASIS format, in line with the technical requirements of the European Agency for Harmonised Harmonised Instrumentation for Standardisation of Processes for Motor Vehicles (EASIS).
The Commission is assisted by a committee to ensure that the information is submitted in a consistent manner.
The directive repeals Directive 70/220/EEC, which was amended by Directive 2004/3/EC and Directive 2001/100/EC.

‘Vehicle emissions’ on the Commission's website.

* GHG emissions: gases emitted by the combustion engine of a motor vehicle.

Summary 167:
Sectoral food law — EU list of authorised substances
Sectoral food law – EU level of protection of human health and consumer protection
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 178/2002 on the European Union’s list of substances
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules to ensure that EU countries’ sectoral food laws ensure that the public is kept informed of the authorised substances in force in the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU sectoral legislation in the area of food.
It does not apply to:
the EU countries themselves;
the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA);
the Member States’ national authorities;
other EU countries and the European Commission.
EU countries must inform the EFSA of the substances they wish to add to the EU list.
The European Commission is responsible for updating and updating the EU lists of substances.
Authorisations
The EU countries must notify the European Authority for Food Safety of any new substances that are added or removed from the list. The list is published in the Official Journal of the EU and is updated by the Commission every 2 years.
An application for an authorisation to add a substance to the list is sent to the Commission by the EU country concerned. The application must contain the following information:
a description of the substance;
a summary of the conditions, specifications or restrictions associated with its presence on the list;
information concerning the application;
details of the procedure for checking the validity of applications;
an opinion on the application.
If an application is rejected, the Commission must inform EU countries of the reasons for its rejection.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
  
It has applied since 20 January 2009 and had to become law in the Member States by 20 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The Commission publishes a list of all the substances on which EU countries may apply for authorisations.
For more information, see:
‘EU list of permitted substances’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Authorised substance: a substance that can be used in the production of foodstuffs, such as meat, milk, eggs, poultry, fish, poultry meat, eggs and meat products.

Summary 168:
EU rules on accreditation, market surveillance, controls of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (European Commission)
EU rules in the field of accreditation and market surveillance
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2002 on the accreditation of conformity assessment bodies performing conformity assessment activities
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules on the organisation and operation of the European Commission’s European accreditation infrastructure for conformity assessment (CE) bodies.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all products covered by the European Union (EU) legislation harmonising the conditions for the marketing of products.
It does not apply to medicines, medicines for human and veterinary use, motor vehicles or motor vehicles and aviation.
EU countries must ensure that national accreditation bodies are independent of commercial conformity assessment* bodies and that they do not compete with them.
National accreditation authorities are responsible for:
monitoring the conformity assessment of products;
assessing whether products are safe for sale;
checking whether they have been affixed with CE marking;
ensuring that the CE mark is correctly affixed on the product;
identifying products that present a risk to human health, safety or the environment;
collecting and disseminating information on products that do not meet the requirements for CE marking.
The European Commission is responsible for setting up the European Rapid Information System (EIS), which allows EU countries to exchange information on the EU accreditation activities.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY?
Decision (EU countries had to incorporate the regulation into national law by 31 December 2002.
   
It entered into force on 1 December 2003.
BACKGROUND
The CE marking is essential for the safe sale of products in the EU.
For more information, see:
‘The EU’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 169:
Arrest warrant agreement between the EU and Norway and Iceland — mutual recognition of arrest warrants
Assessment of the application of the Arrest Warrant Agreement between the European Union and the EU countries and Iceland
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2016/852 — conclusion of the Agreement on mutual recognition and mutual recognition between the Member States and Iceland on the mutual recognition, recognition and recognition of the arrest warrant
Agreement on the Mutual Recognition of Arrest Warrant
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to facilitate the exchange of information between EU countries on the arrest warrants issued for criminal offences.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EU and Iceland are the only countries in the world to have signed an agreement on this type of mutual recognition.
Arrest warrants are issued by one or more EU countries for the arrest of a person who is suspected of committing an offence in another EU country.
An EU country may issue an arrest warrant for a criminal offence if:
the person concerned has committed an offence under the law of the executing country;
the offence for which the warrant has been issued is itself subject to surrender in accordance with the agreement’s provisions;
an EU country has jurisdiction or immunity regarding jurisdiction or execution in the country where the offence is committed;
a person has been extradited to that country from a third country and is protected by provisions of the arrangement under which he or she or he was extradited concerning speciality.
A person is arrested on the basis of an EU arrest warrant if they have been convicted of an offence.
If an EU country does not fulfil the conditions laid down in the agreement, the EU country which issued the warrant may refuse to execute the warrant.
EU countries may refuse the warrant if it does not comply with the conditions of the agreement or if it is not in line with EU law.
When a person in custody is arrested for an offence, the country in which the offence has been committed must immediately inform the issuing country and agree on a new surrender date.
In the event of multiple requests for the execution of the warrant, the executing judicial authority must take a decision on whether the requested person should remain in detention or be handed over to the country of transit. The decision must be taken no later than 30 days after receipt of the request.
Dispute settlement procedure
If a dispute is settled by the parties, the agreement may be terminated.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISIONS APPLY?
Decisions (EU and Iceland) have applied since 1 July 2016.
BACKGROUND
The arrest warrant agreement is one of a number of bilateral agreements between EU and non-EU countries on criminal matters.
For more information, see:
Argentina and Iceland (European External Action Service).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
 
    барсканскиг  гарандскова гласк граста  вашин городск  дальна бести блаксанна (European Commission) — Decision (EU, Iceland, Norway and the Kingdom of Norway) on the conclusion, by the European Commission, of the Agreements on mutualrecognition and mutual recognition between the parties to the agreement (OJ L 136, 1.7.2016, pp. 1-2)
Agreements between the countries of the European Economic Area (EEA) and the European Free Trade Association (EFTA) (European Economic Area) (EEA) (OEA) are one of the most important legal instruments in the EU for criminal matters, as they allow EU countries to share information on criminal offences and to cooperate in criminal proceedings with each other in order to prevent, investigate and prosecute them.
Agreeing countries must notify each other of any changes to their national laws, procedures or administrative arrangements concerning the application and execution of an agreement under this agreement by 1 July 2017.
Council Decision (EC) No 852/2016 of 20 June 2016 on the signature, on behalf the European Parliament and of the Council, and on the provisional application by the Commission of the Interinstitutional Agreement on a mutual Recognition, Recognition and Common Recognition for Arrest Warrant between the Members of the Community and the Republic of Iceland, of 2 July 2016, on 2 July 2017, on 3 July 2017 and on 4 July 2018, on 5 July 2019, on 6 July 2020, on 7 July 2020 and on 9 July 2021, on 10 July 2021 respectively, on 11 July 2021 and on 12 July 2022, on the signing by the EU, Iceland and Norway of a mutual recognition agreement between 2 Member States to be concluded by 2 July 2021 on the common recognition



Summary 170:
Rail passenger services — common rules for the carriage of passengers and their baggage by rail (Regulation (EC) No 852/2006)
Rail passenger service — common ways of handling passengers
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2016/852/EC on common rules on the carriage by rail of passengers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE DECISION?
The regulation aims to ensure that passengers travelling by rail in the European Union are treated equally by rail carriers.
The decision sets out common rules to ensure the protection of passengers’ personal data and the free movement of such data on rail passenger services across the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
This regulation applies to all rail passenger passenger services throughout the EU, with the exception of certain provisions which should apply to urban, suburban and regional passenger services.
It does not apply to:
the carriage of goods by rail;
the ticketing of passengers;
travel information and reservation systems;
information to disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility;
disputes between railway undertakings and ticket vendors.
EU countries may grant exemptions from the application of the provisions of this regulation to domestic rail passenger service.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISIONS APPLY?
Decisions (EU, EU countries and the European Commission have to incorporate the regulation into national law by 31 December 2016.

Summary 171:
European Union statistics in the field of education and lifelong learning — common framework for the production of EU statistics
European Union (EU) statistics on education and long-term care
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2005 on the common production of European Union statistics on the European Union’s education and training systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It establishes a common framework to produce EU statistics on EU countries’ education and learning systems.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries, including the European Commission (Eurostat) and the European Statistical Programme Committee (Euroatom).
It covers the following areas:
education and training (e.g. primary, secondary and tertiary education);
vocational education (vocational training, vocational training, apprenticeships and apprenticeships);
health and social care;
social protection;
employment.
It does not apply to:
employment and social security statistics;
income and living conditions statistics.
Data collection
EU countries must provide Eurostat with data on:
the number of students in each EU country and the number of teachers in each country;
the total number of pupils in each school;
participation of parents in the school system;
children and adolescents in school and in the family;
ages of children and adolescents.
The data must be collected in the form of a sample survey.
Eurostat must collect data on the same as national statistics on income and social protection statistics (i.e. the total income, social security, social protection, employment and health statistics and the social protection indicators.
National data sources
National authorities must send Eurostat a request for information on the data they collect. The data request must be sent to Eurostat by the national authorities in accordance with the specifications of the data request and any other information which is essential for the interpretation of data and the compilation of comparable indicators. Data sources and sample size
The European Commission must collect the data from national authorities by means of a sampling survey. The Commission may also use administrative data sources to reduce the burden on respondents.
If national authorities do not comply with the requirements of the regulation, Eurostat may carry out pilot studies to assess whether the data should be collected or not. These studies must be completed on a voluntary basis by the EU countries.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
 The Lisbon Strategy for Europe is a key element in developing and promoting a skilled, trained and adaptable workforce.
For more information, see:
‘Education and training’ on Eurostat's website.

Summary 172:
EU energy statistics — renewable energy and energy from waste (EU EEA)
EU energy data — renewable and non-renewable energy
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2014 on energy statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the reporting of EU energy statistics.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out how EU countries’ energy statistics are calculated and how they are used to calculate the EU’s energy supply and consumption.
It also sets out rules for calculating the energy used by EU countries in the energy sector.
EU countries must report on the following:
energy production and consumption statistics
energy consumption statistics and final energy consumption statistics for the period from 1 January 2014 to 31 December 2016
energy supply statistics
Energy statistics
The European Commission is responsible for compiling the energy statistics for each EU country.
The EU EEA is the sole source of data for the EU on energy production, consumption and energy consumption for the European Union (EU).
It is the only source of information for EU countries on their energy consumption and for their energy supply.

TANSPARENTS
The EEA defines the following categories of energy producers:
Main activity producer: enterprises, both privately or publicly owned enterprises, which generate electricity, heat or other energy for sale, as their principal activity.
Energy producing industries: enterprises that generate electricity or heat, which operate a thermal power plant, which generates heat or electricity, which is used for heating or cooling, or which operates a heat plant, that generates electricity or electricity for sale.
Other sectors:
Sectors not specifically mentioned or not belonging to energy, industry or transport must be reported as consumption in the EEA;
other sectors: sectors that do not specifically include energy, industries or transport, but which do include energy producing industries;
sectors that are not directly involved in energy production or distribution, but are involved in other sectors, such as agriculture, forestry, fishing, forestry and aquaculture, or in the transport sector;
sectors which are not specifically involved in the production, distribution and distribution of energy, but whose principal activity is to produce, process, process or transport energy;
sectoral sectors that are excluded from the definition of ‘energy producing industries’.

Summary 173:
Non-discrimination and assistance for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility on buses and coaches — rules for non-discriminatory and assistance during their journey
Non-discrimination and assistance on bus and coach travel
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — non-discrimination in the carriage of passengers on public transport
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that passengers travelling by public transport in the EU have the same rights as those of other EU citizens.
It sets out rules for the provision of information and assistance to people with disabilities on the journey.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all public transport, including:
bus and coach services operated by EU countries;
trams and coaches operated by non-EU countries; and
travel agents and tour operators.
EU countries may exempt from the regulation particular regular services because a significant part of such regular services, including at least one scheduled stop, is operated outside the EU.
Accessibility and information
Passengers have the right to:
information regarding the service before and during the journey;
information on the departure and arrival times of the bus or coach;
to change to the corresponding service or to alight from the arriving service for which they have purchased a ticket.
Disabled passengers and persons who have reduced mobility are entitled to information on:
the type of service;
the duration of the journey, including the number of stops and the estimated departure time;
how long the journey is expected to take.
The information must be provided in an equivalent to that provided by other passengers.
Transport companies must ensure that:
all essential information provided to passengers is in an accessible format accessible to disabled passengers;
all information provided by the carrier or terminal managing body is in a language easily understood by the disabled person or person who has reduced mobility;
transport companies are required to provide information to passengers on the type and duration of their journey, the number and type of stops, the distance to the nearest the nearest stop and the distance between the nearest and furthest from the nearest to the destination.
National authorities must take full account of the requirements of consumer protection in general when drawing up their national legislation on the protection of consumers’ rights.
In addition, EU countries must take into account the fact that the United Nations Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities (UNCTAD) sets out the rights of persons with disabilities in relation to their access to public transport.
Amendments to the regulation
Amending Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/853 amends Regulation (EC) No 852/2017 with regard to the introduction of a new type of exemption for certain types of services.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
  данна гарска барка  года   бълакова ванка
 
It has applied since 2 March 2017.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
* Passenger: a person who is physically or mentally disabled or who has a reduced mobility.
* Transport company: a company that operates a public transport service, such as a bus or a coach, that is owned or operated by a person with a disability or who is a member of a group of persons who are physically, mentally or physically disabled or have a disability.

Summary 174:
Aquaculture statistics — EU countries’ data on aquaculture — EU country statistics
Annex I to Regulation (EC) No 788/96 on the production of Community statistics on the Aquaculture sector
Anex II to Regulation(s) No 852/2008 on the collection of EU country data on aquatic species
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 768/2008 establishing a common legal framework for the systematic production of EU statistics on aquaquaculture
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection and compilation of EU countries' aquacultural statistics.
It aims to improve the quality of the EU’s fisheries statistics by harmonising the methods used by EU countries to produce them.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries with a total annual production of more than 1,000 tonnes of fish or molluscs in freshwater and saltwater on their territory.
EU countries must submit a report to the European Commission each year on the total production of fish and shellfish by species.
The Commission is assisted by the Standing Committee for Agricultural Statistics.
Each EU country must submit summary data estimating the total annual total production by species for each year.
A summary report must be sent to the Commission by the end of the calendar year in which the data were collected and compiled.
In addition, EU countries must provide the Commission with a summary report on the number of fish, shellfish and mollusk species they have caught and the total weight of the products they have produced.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYEARS OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The first reference calendar year was 2008.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to encourage the development and management of fisheries, including:
the introduction of a common EU statistical framework for fisheries;
the creation of a single EU statistical system for the production and distribution of fishery statistics;
introduction of a European fishery surveillance system.
For more information, see:
EU fisheries statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Aquatic species: aquatic species are defined as any fish or shellfish that can be caught or caught in freshwater or saltwater.
* Water: water which has a constantly negligible salinity.

Summary 175:
Convention on the management of fisheries in the North-East Atlantic Fisheries Commission (NEAFC) area
CONVENTION ON THE MANAGEMENT OF FISHING RESOURCES IN THE NORTHERN-EAST ATLANTIC FISHERY COMMISSION REGULATION
Decision (EU) 2017/852 on the conclusion of the Convention on the Management of Fishery Resources in the Northern Atlantic FISCO Convention
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE CONVENTION?
The decision and the convention aim to establish a framework for multilateral cooperation on the rational conservation and management of fishery resources in the area defined by the Convention (the Convention Area).
The convention aims to ensure the sustainable management of the fisheries of the north-east Atlantic fisheries in accordance with the principles of the International Labour Organisation (ILO) and the World Health Organization (WHO).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all fishing vessels flying the flag of one or more contracting parties to the convention.
It does not apply to non-contracting parties’ fishing vessels used or intended for use for fishing activities carried out in the convention area.
EU fishing vessels may engage in transhipment activities in the regulatory area only if they have received prior authorisation from the competent authorities in their flag EU country.
Prior notification of entry into port
EU vessels must notify the port country of the vessel’s flag before they enter the area. The port country must inform the flag state of the EU country in which the vessel is registered.
The vessel is required to send a notification to the national authorities of the following:
the list of the fishing resources to be notified;
the total round weight of the fish caught;
a description of the species and the number of tonnes of fish caught.
National authorities must forward a copy of the list to the European Commission or the body designated by it. The Commission forwards this information promptly to the NEAFC Secretary.
Authorisation to land or tranship
Authorisations are issued by national authorities in the EU countries to EU fishing vessels.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
   
The decisions and regulations have applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
The EU is a party to the NEAFC Convention.
For more information, see:
‘The North-Easter Atlantic Fisheries Convention’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 176:
Ecolabel — European Union (EU) ecolabel scheme
Ecolabelling — EU Ecolabel system
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1980/2000 on the European Union’s ecolabelled products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the establishment and application of the voluntary EU environmental label (ecolabel) scheme.
It aims to improve the environmental performance of products and reduce the environmental impact of energy-related products.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all products manufactured in the EU, whether or not they are certified as organic or non-organic.
Eligibility
Products manufactured in a non-EU country may be eligible for the EU environmental labelling if they meet the following criteria:
they meet the relevant product group criteria, i.e. they are manufactured in an EU country;
they are produced in a way that minimises the environmental impacts associated with the product group, based on new or existing life cycle assessment studies.
The European Commission must establish a common register and update it regularly.
Applicants must submit a copy of their annually verified environmental statement to the European Commission. These documents must be submitted to the Commission and the European Ecolabels Board (EUEB).
The Commission must verify that the documents are accurate and that the products meet the requirements of the regulation.
If a product does not meet the criteria, it may prohibit the use of the EU EColabel on that product.
A product may be withdrawn from the market if it does not comply with the required by the regulation or if it is not used in accordance with the regulation's rules.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLACTS APPLYEARLY ENTRY INTO FORCE
Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/852 amends Regulation (EC), which repeals and repeals Regulation (Euratom) No 852/2004.
