Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products — certificate of patent protection (PROCEDURE OF PROTECTIONS OF MEDICINAL PRODUCTS — certificate OFPROVISION OF PROTECTION OF MEDICAL PRODUCTS (PRODUCTS OF PROCEDURES OF PRODUCTS)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1901/2006 on the protection granted by a patent for a new medicinal product
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for the granting of a certificate of protection to medicinal products.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (Euratom) No 2001/82/EC.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all medicinal products that have been granted a patent or authorisation to be placed on the market as a medicinal product in the European Union (EU).
It does not apply to medicines that have not been patented.
The protection granted is limited to the product covered by the patent and the authorisation.
Protection is granted for a period equal to the period which elapsed between the date on which the application for a basic patent was lodged and the date of the first authorisation of the product on the EU market in the Community, reduced by a period of 5 years.
Application for a certificate
The certificate is issued by the competent national authority of the EU country in which the product is located.
An application for the certificate must contain the following information:
the number and date of entry into force of the basic patent;
the product identified in the patent; and
the duration of the certificate.
If the certificate expires, the certificate holder surrenders it or pays an annual fee of €5, which is equivalent to the amount of the patent.
A certificate may be renewed for a further 5 years if the certificate lapses or is invalidated.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?

Summary 178:
Convention on the recognition of judgments in civil and commercial matters (OJ L 347, 29.12.1939, pp. 1-8)
Convention of the Swiss Confederation on the interpretation of judgments (Oj L 347)
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 98/852/EEC on the conclusion of the Convention on the Interpretation of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to harmonise the rules of law in the European Union (EU) countries that are party to the convention.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the European Community (now the EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope of the convention
It applies to all EU countries that have signed or are parties to the Convention.
It does not apply to the EU countries which have not signed or have not yet ratified it.
Jurisdiction
Judgments may be enforced in any EU country where they have been or are to be enforced by the court of the country in which they were or are domiciled.
Judges may only be enforced if they are:
recognised or enforced in the EU country of the consumer’s domicile or in which the contract was concluded;
issued by a person who pursues commercial or professional activities in another EU country;
signed or issued by a company that is based in that EU country or in a country other than the one in which it is based;
executed or concluded in that country.
by a court of that has jurisdiction over claims for limitation of liability arising from the use or operation of a ship or a motor vehicle;
made by an employee of a company based in a non-EU country, or in the territory of an EU country that is a party to a contract with a company or a person whose activities are based in one or more EU countries.
Where a judgment has been granted by a court or tribunal in one EU country and has not been enforced in another, that court has exclusive jurisdiction over that question.
A judgment may not be reviewed as to its substance if it is:
not recognised or enforced;
not enforceable in the country of origin of the judgment;
is not enforceable where it has been or is to be enforceable;
has not been and is not to be recognised in the other EU countries;
may not be enforced where it is enforceable by the courts of the other parties.
In the event of a dispute over the enforcement of a judgment, the judgment may be reviewed only if the parties have not been able to arrange for their defence or have failed to do so.
If the parties are not able to obtain their defence, they may appeal to an EU court or to the European Court of Justice (ECJ).
The ECJ is responsible for determining whether or not the judgment should be enforced. It must give its decision without delay.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
    дарставенна година  Еъланска бода в Луганъ  хиляди и седма  тридесети  
They entered into force on 29 November 1998.
BACKGROUND
 
  Ибральнаг горанка is one of a number of international legal instruments designed to ensure that EU countries’ laws are compatible with those of the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Judgments’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Judgments: a judgment is a legal document that establishes that a person has been convicted of a criminal offence or has been found guilty of a civil offence.
